A general inspection will be conducted at that time. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 4th)

The Panchen Lama Postpones His Trip to Labrang

(Nanjing) The Panchen Lama was originally scheduled to depart from Ta'er Temple on the 23rd day of the third month of the Tibetan calendar to go to Labrang Monastery to chant scriptures and preach. After finishing his business, he would return to Tibet via Xikang. The Panchen Lama's Beijing Office recently received a telegram from the Panchen Lama stating that the climate in Gansu is still cold, the luggage is heavy, and the fodder needed for camels and horses is not ready. Therefore, he has decided to postpone his departure. In addition, Kang Fu'an, the Panchen Lama's representative in Lhasa, came to Beijing from Tibet in January to report on the situation in Tibet to the central government. Recently, due to the Panchen Lama's urgent telegram, he left for Ping (Beiping) at 4:00 PM on the 4th. After staying in Ping for a few days, he will go to Ta'er Temple to meet the Panchen Lama and report, and then return to Tibet with him. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 4th)

Hebei Plans Four Districts to Suppress Bandits

(Baoding) Hebei plans four districts to suppress bandits: District 1 includes 17 counties from Pinghan, Qianxi, Xushui, Mancheng to Jingxing; District 2 includes 7 counties such as Wanxian and Lincheng; District 3 includes Shunde and Yifu; District 4 extends south from Laishui and Yixian across the Pinghan Railway Line. The district commanders are Wang Qifeng for District 1, Lin Zuozhen for District 2, Huang Guanghua for District 3, and Zhao Dengyu for District 4. Each district is divided into four or five sub-districts. The commander of the Second Sub-district of District 1 is Cong Zhaolin. On the 3rd, he convened a meeting of the county magistrates of Qingfan, Wanxian, Tangxian, Wangdu, Dingxian, and Xinle to discuss thorough anti-communist measures. It was decided to start with a thorough household registration check, the construction of blockhouses, and anti-communist propaganda. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 4th)

Japanese Troops in Qian'an Rotate

(Tianjin) The Japanese troops in Qian'an are rotating. Eighty new soldiers have arrived, and the old soldiers, led by Captain Sakata, will sail from Qinhuangdao on the 5th to return to their country. (Special dispatch on the 4th)

The Japanese Side Prepares to Invest 10 Million in Shandong

(Tianjin) The Xingzhong Corporation has drafted a plan to promote railways in North China. The plan was submitted by Director Shihe to the Tokyo headquarters and assigned to the resident representatives in Ping, Jin, Ji, Hu, and Yue, as well as employees of the South Manchuria Railway, for preliminary investigation. It was decided to develop the project. The Japanese side plans to invest 10 million in Shandong, with the South Manchuria Railway, Xingzhong Corporation, Mitsubishi, and Mitsui responsible for raising the funds. The funds will be divided as follows: 1. Spinning industry, investing 3 million yuan to build large spinning mills in Weixian, Liaocheng, and Jining; 2. Wool spinning mill, investing 400,000 yuan; 3. Weaving and dyeing mill, investing 1.5 million yuan; 4. Machine manufacturing factory, investing 500,000 yuan; 5. Beverage factory, such as manufacturing soy sauce, wine, and canned goods, investing 500,000 yuan; 6. Paper factory, using locally produced bark and grass as raw materials, investing 4.5 million yuan. The Xingzhong Corporation will investigate the situation and then submit a plan to the Ministry of Colonial Affairs, Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Army, and Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry. A meeting will be held by the four provinces to decide on the plan before gradually implementing it. (Special dispatch on the 4th)

The Tianjin Sino-Japanese Health Exhibition Opened Yesterday

(Tianjin) The Sino-Japanese Health Exhibition opened on the 4th. At 2:00 PM, a ceremony was held inside the Municipal Party Headquarters. More than 500 Chinese and foreign guests, including Tada, Nagami, Kubota, and Consul Anishi, attended. Mayor Xiao presided over the meeting and delivered the opening speech. Li Zaizhong, Director of the Health Bureau, reported on the preparations. Consul Anishi delivered a speech on behalf of Kawagoe. Later, Li Tingyu, President of the South Manchuria Railway Medical College, also gave speeches. At 3:00 PM, photos were taken. Afterwards, the attendees went to the National Goods Exhibition Hall. Mayor Xiao cut the ribbon and opened the exhibition to the public. More than 1,000 pictures and models were on display, which were quite eye-catching. The exhibition will last until the 18th. The Beining Railway will offer special discounts during the exhibition to attract visitors from afar. (Special dispatch on the 4th)

Agreed on Measures to Reorganize the Daokou-Qinghua Railway Loan

(Nanjing) The British bondholders of the Daokou-Qinghua Railway loan have not been repaid on schedule due to the railway's insufficient revenue. In order to maintain China's foreign creditworthiness, the Ministry of Railways has long been determined to reorganize the loan. After lengthy negotiations with the British side, three reorganization methods have been agreed upon. The London Council of Foreign Bondholders and the Fu Company have requested bondholders to accept the methods, and it is scheduled to be announced in Nanjing and London on the 5th. The original text of the methods is as follows: 1. Interest payment method: From 1936 to 1938, interest will be paid at 2.5% per annum. However, if the Daokou-Qinghua Railway's annual cash surplus within three years is sufficient to cover all debt principal and interest payments (including the principal and interest of this loan), the interest on this loan can be increased to a maximum of 5%. From 1939 onwards, annual interest will be paid at 5%. 2. Principal repayment method: The principal of this loan totals £495,700. Starting in July 1936, it will be repaid in installments over a period of 27 years. 3. Elimination of overdue interest method: Bondholders agree to waive four-fifths of the overdue interest. The un-waived portion will be reissued as interest-free small notes, which will be paid after the principal of this loan is fully repaid after 1966. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 4th)

Economic Committee Orders Efforts to Strengthen Dikes

The Executive Yuan Orders All Provincial Governments to Comply

(Nanjing) With the flood season approaching, the Economic Committee issued orders to the Yellow River and Yangtze River Water Commissions on the 4th, earnestly admonishing them to immediately consult with the provinces along the Yellow River and Yangtze River to strengthen the dikes and take practical flood prevention measures in order to eliminate disasters and avoid the danger of breaches. It also ordered them to provide a list of the positions and names of the personnel responsible for flood prevention in each province along the Yellow River and Yangtze River for record keeping. Any negligence will be the sole responsibility of the personnel in charge. At the same time, it has sent a letter to the Executive Yuan to order the provincial governments of Hebei, Shandong, Henan, Hubei, Hunan, Anhui, and Jiangxi to strictly comply in order to emphasize flood prevention and avoid negligence. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 4th)

Page 6

The Ethiopian Emperor Takes His Family on a British Warship and Leaves the Country for Palestine. Entrusting Power to the Cabinet is Not Abdication. Rumor that He Intends for Ethiopia to Conduct Peace Negotiations for the Surrender of the City

(London) British Foreign Secretary Eden declared in the House of Commons today that the Ethiopian Emperor and his entourage have departed from Djibouti today on the British cruiser "HMS Enterprise" bound for the port of Haifa in Palestine.

On Friday evening, the Ethiopian Emperor told British Minister Sir Barton that he had relinquished power and entrusted it to the cabinet. The Emperor also wished to take his family to Palestine. The British government felt obliged to comply with this request, and therefore dispatched the cruiser "HMS Enterprise" to Djibouti to transport the Emperor directly to the port of Haifa. It is expected to depart at 6:00 PM tonight (local time). The British government naturally hopes that the Emperor will not be involved in the war while residing in Palestine. The Foreign Secretary deeply praised the members of the British Legation in the Ethiopian capital for their resourceful handling of the dangerous situation, and acknowledged that British Minister Sir Barton had been tireless in his work. His praise cannot be expressed merely through commendation. A company of Indian soldiers stationed at the British Legation saved many lives and their bravery is commendable. The British expatriates in the Ethiopian capital repeatedly risked their lives to rescue Europeans and other people in times of emergency, demonstrating commendable courage. (Reuters dispatch on the 4th)

(London) It was learned today that before leaving the capital, the Ethiopian Emperor had requested the British to leave a warship anchored in Djibouti for his use. The Emperor also stated that he had entrusted his power to the Ethiopian government, but this did not mean formal abdication. The British government has agreed to his request. It is not yet known, but two British destroyers have indeed sailed from Aden, one of which is heading to Djibouti. The Emperor's request has created a difficult situation. Will Italy be happy to see the Emperor? Will it object to the British warship taking him away? It is believed that this is what the British must consider when deciding to send a warship for his use. It is reported that France is prepared to welcome the Emperor to reside in France, provided that he does not engage in any attempts to interfere with the war. (Reuters dispatch on the 4th)

(London) In the interest of the Ethiopian Emperor's future and maintaining the League of Nations' sanctions front, Britain conducted urgent negotiations with France today. Foreign Secretary Eden stated that the Ethiopian Emperor is the head of a state, the commander-in-chief of the Ethiopian army, and a member of the League of Nations, therefore neutral countries should not treat him as a prisoner. Well-informed observers believe that Britain and France will convene a three-power conference including Italy to resolve the Ethiopian issue. (National Telegram on the 4th)

(Rome) Unconfirmed reports received here today indicate that the Italian army's delayed entry into the Ethiopian capital is due to peace negotiations for the surrender of the city. The Italian authorities naturally wish to formally enter the city after reaching a negotiated compromise, rather than taking it by force. It is not yet known who from the Ethiopian side is participating in the negotiations. According to rumors several days ago, the mayor and police chief of the Ethiopian capital and another official planned to greet the Italian army a few miles outside the city. (Reuters dispatch on the 4th)

(Paris) French political circles are currently unaware of the Ethiopian Emperor's whereabouts. It is reported that before leaving the capital, the Emperor expressed his desire to travel to land under the British flag. If the Emperor wishes to go to French Somaliland, the French authorities there will treat him with due respect and he is free to stay or leave as he pleases. (Reuters dispatch on the 4th)

Resisting a Powerful Enemy, the Ethiopian Emperor is Glorious Even in Defeat

The Port of Djibouti is Saluted by the People

The Governor of Somalia Treats Him as a Distinguished Guest

Djibouti: The Ethiopian Emperor and his entourage are still stationed in Djibouti and did not depart by ship yesterday. They may depart today, but their destination is currently unknown. It is speculated that they will first go to Aden and then to London. When the Emperor and his entourage arrived here yesterday, the Governor of Djibouti and his entourage were all dressed in formal attire, and the commander of the French garrison and other high-ranking officials, along with a company of Filipino soldiers, stood in double file on the platform to greet him. There were only a few onlookers at the station because very few people knew of the Emperor's arrival. After the Emperor's family arrived, they took vehicles prepared by the French Governor to the Governor's residence. Filipino soldiers were stationed along the route to provide security. After the news of the Emperor's arrival spread, several hundred people gathered in front of the Governor's residence, hoping to catch a glimpse of the Emperor. Many of the onlookers shed tears for the Emperor's loss of his country and exile. When a part of the Emperor's entourage arrived at the Ethiopian consulate here, an incident occurred. An Italian tried to take a photograph, but was stopped by an Ethiopian, resulting in a fistfight between the two. (Reuters dispatch on the 4th)

French Port of Djibouti: The Ethiopian Emperor and a party of more than twenty members of the imperial family will leave here tomorrow morning, most likely on the British destroyer "Diana" bound for the port of Aden. It is generally believed that the Emperor may travel from Aden to Britain. The Emperor's special train arrived here at 2 p.m. today, later than scheduled, having been delayed for some time en route, the reason for which is unknown. The Governor of French Somaliland and local senior civil and military officials were waiting at the station. From the station platform to the Governor's residence, Senegalese soldiers were stationed along the route to prevent passers-by from approaching. After the train arrived, the soldiers played music to pay their respects. The Empress, her face covered with a thick veil, got off the train first, followed by the Emperor, who was dressed in white, without a hat, and looked very tired. He refused to make a statement and asked French officials not to allow reporters and photographers to approach. He then went to the Governor's residence in the same car with Prince Makonnen and the Governor of Somaliland. The Empress, Crown Prince Asfaw Wossen, and the commander of the French garrison followed in the second car. The people along the way were moved to see the Emperor's countenance and cheered to show their respect. After the Emperor and his entourage arrived at the Governor's residence, they had a light meal, having not eaten since last night, and then retired to their rooms to rest. Foreign Minister Hailu, Northern Commander General Gasser, and others also came with the Emperor. (Havas dispatch on the 4th)

Djibouti: The Governor of French Somaliland visited Yasu, the grandson of former Ethiopian Emperor Menelik, in the town of Tadjoura this afternoon after receiving the Ethiopian Emperor and his party. He returned here in the evening. (Note: Yasu succeeded Menelik after his death, but was deposed and imprisoned in the mountains for being incompetent and useless. Emperor Haile Selassie was replaced by Ras Tafari after being deposed. He has been imprisoned for twenty years. It is heard that as the Emperor was defeated and exiled, Italy plans to install Yasu as the new Emperor of Ethiopia.) The local authorities have taken various measures to prevent incidents from occurring during the Emperor's stay. The wireless telephone between here and the Ethiopian capital has been out of service since last night. It is said that the streets there are littered with corpses. After the riots, two factions are vying for power, one led by General Ayarra, the governor of the northernmost province, and the other led by General Wason. Wason was the head of the government after the Emperor's exile. (Havas dispatch on the 3rd)

Climbing Mountains and Crossing Ridges, Italian Troops Approach the Ethiopian Capital

Heavy Rain Hampers the Advance

The Southern Army Occupies Jijiga

(Rome) According to news received today, Italian troops have occupied the mountains seven miles from the Ethiopian capital. The Commander-in-Chief of the Italian Army is stationed in Debre Berhan, ninety miles from the Ethiopian capital. A formal entry ceremony will be held soon. Yesterday, the Italian Army's supply train climbed Mount Tumassa. The mountain road was rugged and the train was halted for a day. More than a thousand heavy vehicles have crossed the mountain, but have been damaged. The food needed by the Commander-in-Chief and others is being transported by plane. (Reuters dispatch on the 4th)

Italian Army Front in the North: Italian Askari native troops occupied Mount Entoto today. This mountain overlooks the Ethiopian capital. The Commander-in-Chief of the Italian Army is leading the troops to continue the advance and has established a headquarters in Debre Berhan. They may enter the Ethiopian capital at any time. A motorized army of 1,000 vehicles has passed the last peak and reached the plateau today. The Ethiopian capital is located on this plateau, but it is still at least 120 miles away from the capital. (National Report on the 3rd)

(Paris) According to news from the Ethiopian capital, heavy rain is falling in the suburbs, and many roads have been washed away. The Italian troops advancing towards the capital have been hampered, and may not be able to reach the capital until tomorrow. (Havas dispatch on the 3rd)

Djibouti: It has been learned here that General Graziani's Italian Somaliland troops have defeated General Nasibu's troops and occupied Jijiga. (National Telegram on the 3rd)

(Rome) A communiqué was issued here today stating that a mechanized column of the Italian army has occupied Debre Berhan, and the vanguard is forty kilometers away from that location. On the southern front, the vanguard of the Italian army continues to advance, and several Italian detachments have passed Daga Bur, advancing eighty kilometers. Aircraft are very active across the entire front. Residents of the Ogaden province are now welcoming the Italian army. (Reuters dispatch on the 4th)

Soldiers and Bandits Randomly Burn and Loot, Turning the Ethiopian Capital into a Field of Rubble

The Italian Army Will Gain Nothing Upon Entering the City

The Streets Are Desolate, with Corpses Lying Everywhere

Only the Howls of Wild Dogs Can Be Heard, Creating a Bleak Scene

Ethiopian Capital: A Reuters correspondent reports that the Ethiopian capital is a wasteland. Several fires are not yet fully extinguished. Corpses are lying all over the streets. The city center has been completely burned down. The Customs Building is still smoldering. Several armories have exploded. The number of dead and wounded throughout the city cannot be estimated, because most of the people have become murderous and arsonist bandits, determined to leave an empty city for the Italian army. Looking north from the top of a small hill in the British embassy garden, it is said that dust can be seen rising thirty miles away, probably from the vanguard of the Italian army, but this may be slightly delayed by the rain. Currently, only one foreigner has been killed: Mrs. Stanton, a Seventh-day Adventist missionary, was killed by a stray bullet in her residence. Initially, many foreigners went to the American embassy for refuge, but eventually all moved to the British embassy. (National Telegram on the 4th)

Ethiopian Capital: Ethiopian mobs have been looting and killing since Saturday. Today, they attacked the headquarters of the British Red Cross, but were repelled by the director, Mr. Lambie. One Ethiopian was killed and one was injured. The Turkish consulate was also attacked. Afterwards, the Indian infantry from the British embassy arrived and the mobs scattered, leaving twelve bodies behind. Two Reuters correspondents are here. One of Mr. Lorebeau's servants was shot in the leg. When Mr. Eames went out to report the news today, the glass of his car was also pierced by bullets. According to the latest news, the Italian army is now encamped in the Akaki plain, ten miles from the city. White flags are flying atop the earthen houses along the way. The government treasury has been broken into by the mob and looted. Rebellious Gala tribesmen are guarding outside the city. Whenever they see mobs carrying their looted property and trying to escape into the mountains, they attack them. Occasionally, a few Gala tribesmen, armed with spears, enter the city with Gala women dressed as men. By this evening, the city has been slightly quieter. The streets are deserted, and only the howls of wild dogs can be heard as they search for food and corpses. (National Telegram on the 4th)

(Paris) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs recently received a telegram from Ambassador Bodard in Ethiopia, reporting on the situation in the Ethiopian capital. It is said that the chaotic state there is like a revolution. This afternoon, deserters from the front line swarmed into the city, like horses freed from their reins, uncontrollable. They set fire to the palace, shops, and the residences of European expatriates. In an instant, the city was ablaze. These people looted wildly in the midst of the fire. There were also cases of mobsters killing each other. In addition, groups of troublemakers roamed the streets, inciting unrest, determined to destroy everything, so that when the Italian army entered the city, all they would find would be a field of rubble. In the chaos, a total of twenty-four European expatriates were killed. All foreign embassies have now issued curfews. The French embassy is sheltering 1,500 expatriates from sixteen countries, many of whom are women and children. One pregnant woman, about to give birth, fled in panic and gave birth to a baby in the embassy last night. Several other expatriates took refuge at the railway station. The refugees valiantly resisted when Ethiopian rioters came to attack, and were spared. In addition, two French expatriates were suddenly attacked by rioters. Isolated and helpless, they were in great danger. Fortunately, they had weapons, repelled the rioters, and managed to escape to the embassy. Multiple groups of rioters also attacked the front of the embassy, intending to loot it. There were as many as 2,000 rioters, but they were repelled by the embassy's Askari guards. Two expatriates were shot and injured. The French government recently sent a telegram to Ambassador Bodard, praising him for his proper handling of the situation and the calmness of the expatriates. Ambassador Bodard will read the telegram to the public and offer words of comfort to the refugees. (Havas dispatch on the 3rd)

Ethiopian Capital: It is said that the Italian army advanced to the Akaki River, ten miles from the Ethiopian capital, last night, and will enter the city today. The looting and robbery by bandits and scattered soldiers has slightly subsided, but armed bandits have entered the city, endangering the lives of citizens and expatriates. British expatriates, except for a few Arabs who have erected barriers in their homes to defend themselves, are all residing peacefully in the British embassy and elsewhere. Expatriates of twenty-three nationalities are taking refuge in the British embassy. The embassy was attacked by bandits armed with rifles and machine guns. After resisting for several hours, the embassy staff decided to leave the embassy. With the help of the British embassy guards, they safely escaped. It is estimated that a total of ten Europeans in the Ethiopian capital have been killed, mostly of Greek and Armenian nationality. Yesterday, the British embassy's rescue team recovered more than 300 wounded Ethiopians in the city. A group of Ethiopian bandits, in a streetcar loaded with valuables, went to the British embassy and offered to sell them back to the original owners. The entire carload of goods was confiscated by the British embassy. A young man was rescued and taken to the British embassy. He said that his residence was surrounded by a large group of bandits, who had several machine guns. He and two companions resisted until they ran out of ammunition. The three of them killed twenty bandits before running out of ammunition, and then escaped on a rescue team's heavy truck. Bandits surrounded the Bank of Abyssinia for several hours. The bank's employees and servants fought bravely. Later, with the protection of the guards, they were able to reach the British embassy. Ethiopians are still looting and randomly firing shots into the air. Several fires have broken out again in the city. In addition, today there is heavy rain, making the refugees even more miserable. (Reuters dispatch on the 4th)

American Expatriates Seek Refuge in the British Embassy

(Washington) According to a telegram from Mr. Engebretson, the American Chargé d'Affaires in Ethiopia, although gunfire continued incessantly last night, it was slightly quieter by dawn. American expatriate women and children in Ethiopia have now sought refuge in the British embassy from the American embassy. (National Telegram on the 3rd)

(Washington) The 250 Indian troops stationed in the Ethiopian capital, led by British officers, are providing great comfort to the expatriates there. The Indian troops come to the rescue of any expatriates of any nationality who are in danger and ask for their help. Recently, women who had taken refuge in the American embassy were transported in three large cars to the more heavily defended British military camp, escorted by Indian troops along the way. (Reuters dispatch on the 4th)

Two Attacks on the French Legation

(Paris) The French Minister to Abyssinia, Mr. Bapst, telegraphed today reporting that the French Legation in the Abyssinian capital was attacked twice on Saturday morning, injuring two Europeans. Furthermore, bandits set fire to the warehouses of the Djibouti Railway on the same afternoon, with total losses to French nationals estimated at millions of francs. (3rd, National Telegram)

(Paris) According to a recent prepaid telegram from the French Minister to Abyssinia, Mr. Bodard, in the Abyssinian capital, French nationals at the French Legation and the railway station were subjected to fierce attacks by Abyssinian rioters. The French Legation was targeted by Abyssinians twice, suffering thousands of bullet hits. Fortunately, a shelter had been dug in the legation in recent months, so the women and children were unharmed. Although food and water supplies are sufficient in the French Legation, there is a severe shortage of ammunition. The Abyssinian Youth Party warned the French Legation that the Abyssinian people would continue to attack the legation. French nationals taking refuge at the station were also besieged by Abyssinian rioters, a situation that is particularly worrying. (3rd, National Telegram)

Twenty-Five Foreign Nationals Killed

(London) It is reported that after the Abyssinian King fled, a total of twenty-five foreign nationals were killed in the riots in the Abyssinian capital, including one American woman. According to Djibouti sources, twenty-four Greeks and Armenians lost their lives while defending their shops against looters. The American woman, the wife of Dr. Stating, was struck by a stray bullet and died instantly. (4th, Reuters Telegram)

British Cabinet Special Meeting

(London) The British Cabinet held a special meeting today to consider: the developments in Abyssinia; the submission to Hitler of his peace proposals; the leak of the budget secrets, (which made the public prepare insurance against the increase of tea tax and income tax at the last minute). The Chancellor of the Exchequer, Mr. Chamberlain, will make a statement in the House of Commons today regarding the leak of the budget secrets. Due to the changing situation in Abyssinia, the Foreign Office was very active yesterday afternoon. Foreign Secretary Eden, who had gone to the countryside, has returned to the city, taking a streetcar to the Foreign Office to consult with officials. Prime Minister Baldwin, who was resting in Chequers, also returned to 10 Downing Street at 4:00 PM.

The Abyssinian King boarded a British destroyer and sailed to an unknown location. The British authorities have given their approval. It is said that after the Abyssinian King fled, a British destroyer was sent to Djibouti to provide the British Consul with rapid transportation. The Abyssinian King's future plans depend partly on his own wishes and partly on the wishes of the French government, as the Abyssinian King is now a guest of the French government. The British government is currently consulting with the French government on this matter. London has not yet heard of the Abyssinian King's formal abdication. When the Abyssinian King left the Abyssinian capital, he handed over the government's powers to his cabinet members. (4th, Reuters Telegram)

British Ships Stationed in Gibraltar Set Sail for the Mediterranean

Gibraltar, British Territory - Official sources here have announced that the 20th Destroyer Flotilla, belonging to the British Home Fleet and currently stationed here, has been ordered by Admiral Dreyer, Commander-in-Chief of the Mediterranean Fleet, to set sail for the eastern Mediterranean as soon as possible. (4th, Havas Telegram)

Increased Ship Dues for the Suez Canal

New Contract Between Egypt and the Canal Company

(Cairo) Today, a decree signed by the late King Fuad of Egypt regarding the contract between the Egyptian government and the Suez Canal Company was published. The maximum ship dues for vessels passing through the canal, which was 36 piasters per ton, will now be increased by 63 piasters (10 gold francs). This is because Egypt recently announced the abolition of the gold standard, and the value of the Egyptian currency is calculated in gold. It is feared that it will depreciate, so the ship dues are increased to avoid losses to the Suez Canal Company due to the depreciation of the currency. The company has agreed to allow two Egyptians to join the company's board of directors and has decided that Egyptians will account for one-quarter of the company's employees. (3rd, Reuters Telegram)

French Chamber of Deputies Re-election Results: Victory for the Left-Wing Front

Socialist Party Holds an Absolute Majority of Seats

Communist Party Increases Fourfold, an Unexpected Development

Radical Party's Position is Pivotal

(Paris) The second round of voting in the Chamber of Deputies re-election concluded yesterday. Of the 618 seats, 614 have been officially announced, and the distribution is determined as follows: Left-Wing People's Front - 378 seats: (A) Communist Party (including independent Communists) 82 seats; (B) Orthodox Socialist Party 146 seats; (C) Republican Socialist Union Party 15 seats; (D) Independent Socialist Party 10 seats; (E) Radical Socialist Party 115 seats. Center Faction - 137 seats: (A) Independent Radical Party 31 seats; (B) Left-Wing Republican Party 83 seats; (C) People's Democratic Party 23 seats. Right-Wing National Front - 99 seats: (A) Republican Democratic Union Party 88 seats; (B) Conservative Party 11 seats.

The parties belonging to the Left-Wing People's Front won a total of 39 seats in the 60 constituencies of Paris and its suburbs, of which 32 seats belong to the Communist Party. (4th, Havas Telegram)

(Paris) As of 1:30 AM this morning, the results of the Chamber of Deputies re-election showed that of the 618 seats, 614 have been announced. The rate of increase in the number of seats for the parties of the Left-Wing People's Front far exceeded expectations, and the leftward shift of the new Chamber of Deputies is undoubtedly confirmed. The number of seats for the Orthodox Socialist Party was only 96 in the previous Chamber, but has now increased to 146, making it the party with the most seats, which can be called a pioneering event in the history of the French Republic. Other socialist parties, such as the Republican Socialist Union Party, which holds 25 seats, and the Independent Socialist Party, which holds 10 seats, when added to the seats won by the Orthodox Socialist Party, total 181 seats, and will occupy the largest force in the new Chamber of Deputies. It has been 20 years since the Radical Socialist Party was the largest party in the Chamber, and now its position has been taken over by the socialist parties, which is a characteristic of this election result. Furthermore, the Communist Party, including the independent Communist Party, only held 20 seats in the previous Chamber of Deputies, but has now increased to 81 seats, becoming one of the largest parties in the new Chamber, which is also most noteworthy. As for the Radical Socialist Party, which held 160 seats in the previous Chamber of Deputies, it has now decreased to 108 seats, and has retreated to the position of the Orthodox Socialist Party, its losses are comparable to those of the right-wing parties. However, the party still occupies a position of influencing the political situation in the new Chamber. Generally speaking, when a future left-wing cabinet is formed, if it is influenced by the Communist Party, at least half of the Radical Socialist Party members will vote against the new cabinet. Fortunately, the Communist Party has already stated that if the new cabinet is organized by the Socialist Party, it does not intend to participate, so the Radical Socialist Party may not make things difficult for the new cabinet. However, the Communist Party has also stated that if the new cabinet's domestic and foreign policies are in line with the minimum program of the Left-Wing People's Front, the party will provide assistance. According to political figures, France's foreign policy in the future will not undergo any substantial changes, but the influence of the Communist Party members may make the cooperation between France and the Soviet Union closer. As for economic and financial aspects, since Marxist members occupy more than one-third of the seats in the new Chamber, it is possible that the legal system for all social undertakings will be changed. Prime Minister Sarraut will continue to serve until May 31, and then resign with his entire cabinet to President Lebrun. At that time, the President will entrust the leader of the Orthodox Socialist Party, Leon Blum, to form a new cabinet in accordance with the Constitution. It is not yet known whether he will be appointed, but in any case, there is no doubt that the new cabinet will have socialist participation (note that the party has always refused to participate in the cabinet, only making an exception to join the cabinet during the European War). The Sarraut cabinet is now scheduled to hold an important meeting on Tuesday (May 5) to discuss the political situation after the Chamber of Deputies re-election. (4th, Havas Telegram)

Sarraut Cabinet Shaken

Socialist Party Prepares to Take Over Power

(Paris) The Communist Party's great victory in this Chamber of Deputies re-election has threatened the Sarraut cabinet. Prime Minister Sarraut is now scheduled to convene an emergency cabinet meeting on Tuesday, because cabinet members Sutoen and Dede have both failed in the election, and Gunode and Niger have also been defeated, so there are already four cabinet members who cannot serve. (3rd, National Telegram)

(Paris) After the conclusion and announcement of the second round of voting in the Chamber of Deputies election, the Orthodox Socialist Party has become the largest party. The party leader, Leon Blum, recently published an article in the party newspaper "People's Daily," which stated: "After the victory of our party, we are now prepared to fulfill our mission. What is the mission? It is to organize and lead the new cabinet of the People's Front." Our party has the most seats in the new Chamber of Deputies compared to other parties, and is in the middle position between the other two parties of the People's Front, namely the Communist Party and the Radical Socialist Party, so we should obtain power. (4th, Havas Telegram)

Herriot Has Been Elected

(Paris) In the second round of voting in the Chamber of Deputies re-election, the Mayor of Lyon and former leader of the Radical Socialist Party, Herriot, has been elected. Others who have been elected include former Finance Minister Leino (who advocated the devaluation of the franc), Speaker of the Chamber of Deputies Puisson, one of the leaders of the Left-Wing People's Front, Pesseley, and the leader of the Independent Communist Party, Doriot. However, the leader of the Right-Wing National Front, Puyong, and the current Minister of Aviation, Tea (Radical Socialist Party), have been defeated. (4th, Havas Telegram)

Stock Market Prices Plunge

(Paris) After the announcement of the results of the second round of voting in the Chamber of Deputies election, the stock market has experienced adverse effects. French government bonds and Bank of France stocks have fallen sharply, while foreign securities have risen sharply. Bank of France stock has fallen from 7250 points to 6500 points, and French government bonds have fallen from 67.05 points to 65.45 points. (4th, Havas Telegram)

Britain Watches French Political Situation

(London) Londoners are now watching developments in France, believing that if the general public panics upon seeing the left wing's election victory, it will force the franc to break away from the gold standard before a new cabinet is formed. Therefore, the future of the French currency will depend on the attitude of the general public. However, some people also say that most of those who voted for the left wing yesterday were ordinary people, and they may not panic suddenly on Sunday. The sale of francs this morning is the most seen in recent years. When the French exchange rate was 75.27, the British Equalization Fund wanted to maintain it again, but it still failed to stop the selling pressure. The British Equalization Fund has purchased a large amount of gold, so a question has been raised: How long can the British authorities maintain the French currency? Because the gold purchased by the Equalization Fund has now reached its saturation point. It is reported that a large amount of cash was transported to New York again today. The Board of Directors of the Bank of France has now convened a special meeting to discuss the overall situation. (4th, Reuters Telegram)

France Sends Troops Along Railway Line

Djibouti - The authorities here dispatched two companies of Senegalese infantry by train last night to the Abyssinian capital in order to protect the railway station there (the railway from Djibouti Port to the Abyssinian capital is operated by France). According to recent news from the Abyssinian capital, the situation there has now improved. Also, it is now known that of the Europeans who died in the turmoil yesterday, all twenty-four were Greek or Armenian merchants who were killed because their shops were looted by rioters and they resisted desperately. (4th, Havas Telegram)

Sir Frederick Leith-Ross Returns to England to Discuss China's Political and Economic Progress; Achievements of the Central Government Increase Daily; Financial Prospects Show Obvious Improvement

Sir Frederick Scheduled to Take Up New Post as Foreign Under-Secretary in Mid-July

(London) The former British Ambassador to China, Sir Frederick Leith-Ross, returned here last night with his wife and children to take up the post of Foreign Under-Secretary. In a conversation with a Reuters reporter, he said that the achievements of the Chinese Central Government are increasing daily, which is a prominent feature of the Chinese situation. President Chiang Kai-shek is very admirable and has great ability, never slacking off. He is a statesman and a true patriot. The economic work done by the Nanjing government is very obvious, and the financial prospects are also showing improvement. He believes that China's new currency system can be successful, and the Central Bank's power to stabilize the currency is also extremely important. The rural situation, at least in central China, is gradually improving. Although low prices have burdened farmers, and irregular taxes are still too high, farmers are no longer suffering the pain of having all their assets swallowed up by greedy and brutal warlords. China has a vast territory and lacks transportation, so although the Communist bandits have been greatly reduced, they are still a serious problem. The students' unrest originates from hostility towards Japan, and university authorities are very worried. However, this kind of situation exists in many countries. The recent talks between student representatives and President Chiang have cleared the air a lot. The New Life Movement is a very interesting phenomenon. Some of its tenets may not be necessary in the eyes of foreigners, but basically, it originates from the deepest things in Chinese culture, so it is obviously a starting point and a legitimate goal in the work of national revival. As for the future, of course, much depends on Sino-Japanese relations. Although he is now happy to return home, he enjoyed his two years in China very much. His life in China was very interesting. He now brings many happy ideas with him, the most important of which is his confidence in China's goodwill towards England. Sir Frederick will have a short vacation and is scheduled to take up his new post in mid-July. (4th, Reuters Telegram)

Achievements of Li Hongguang, a Leader of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteers

His Troops Expanded to More Than 5,000 Men

Repeatedly Launched Successful Attacks on Japanese and Puppet Troops

(Harbin) The troops led by anti-Japanese volunteer leader Li Hongguang have expanded to more than 5,000 men, scattered throughout the eastern Jilin region, including the areas of Dasuifen River, Hulin, Changbai Mountain, and Batonggou. Since January, they have repeatedly launched successful attacks on Japanese and puppet troops. It is reported that on April 10, about 2,000 men from his unit surrounded the county seat of Dongxing, engaged in a fierce battle for 20 hours, and captured more than 10 cannons. On the 19th, they occupied the town of Gucheng, and a puppet army regiment was killed and its commander surrendered and defected. On the 23rd, the unit ambushed a puppet army supply train in Batonggou, capturing countless grain and ammunition. The unit is now extremely active, and hundreds of farmers are joining its ranks with weapons every day. (8th, China United Press Telegram)

Japanese Inspection Group and Siamese Government Secretly Discuss Canal Excavation

Cooperation Draft Proposed

(Hong Kong) Bangkok dispatch: According to reliable sources, the Japanese economic inspection group sent to Siam represented the Japanese authorities in Siam to secretly discuss the issue of opening the Kra Canal with the Siamese government, and has drafted a cooperation draft to be taken back to Tokyo for further consideration. The group left Siam on April 20. Before leaving, the group leader, Yasukawa Yunosuke, told reporters that the group's trip had achieved the purpose of Japanese-Siamese friendship, and that relations between the two countries would become closer in the future. Planting Alfalfa to Reduce Siltation in the Yellow River

The Economic Commission Establishes an Alfalfa Seed Nursery in Suiyuan

(Nanjing) The Economic Commission believes that the problem of the Yellow River lies in the siltation, and the source of siltation is due to the erosion of the loess slopes in the northwest. In order to prevent erosion, while preparing a fundamental plan, it will first widely plant alfalfa in the upper reaches of the Yellow River. The northwest climate is dry, and trees are not easy to grow, and the area is too large, so planting trees cannot be universal in a short time. However, alfalfa is drought-resistant and does not require irrigation, and it can grow and reproduce. Moreover, the root system is very deep and intertwined, which is more effective in preventing erosion than trees. If the loess slopes in the northwest can be planted extensively, the siltation of the Yellow River can be reduced. The Commission previously ordered the agricultural office to establish an alfalfa seed nursery in Suiyuan, and the office, together with the Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission, sent personnel to the provinces of Henan, Shaanxi, Suiyuan, Shanxi, Ningxia, and Gansu to investigate the geology and livestock feed in order to proceed with the work. According to the reply, the benefits of alfalfa are great, so it should be planted directly and should be actively promoted to achieve universality. Recently, the Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission was ordered to quickly consult with the relevant provincial governments in the upper reaches of the Yellow River to plant it widely, and at the same time, to quickly formulate an engineering plan in order to reduce the siltation of the Yellow River. (4th, Central News Agency Telegram)

Two Ministries Propose Methods to Reorganize the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Debt

(Nanjing) The Ministries of Finance and Railways proposed to discuss the methods of reorganizing the Tianjin-Pukou Railway debt with British and German merchants. From 1936 to March 1938, each pays interest of 2.5% per year. Starting in 1939, the original contract regulations will be restored, and weekly interest of 5% will be paid. Principal repayments will begin in 1940. The amount of principal to be repaid each year will be based on the total cash income of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway. From 1940 to 1942, 1% of the total cash income will be allocated each year. 1.5% will be allocated in 1943, and 2% will be allocated in 1944. Thereafter, it will increase by 0.5% each year, with 10% allocated in 1988 and 12.5% ​​allocated annually from 1989 until the principal is paid off. We also reserve the right to propose the repayment of principal. (4th, Special Dispatch)

Reuters Special Business Report, May 4th

Gold and Silver

London The unstable French political situation caused the London gold price to loosen by sixpence, to 140 shillings and fourpence. It is reported that the Bank of France will have £3 million worth of gold carried to the United States by the French ship "Nordique" this Wednesday.

London Big Article Today the silver market is stable, with spot and futures prices both at 20 pence 375, up 125 each. India bought in, and China and speculators engaged in both buying and selling.

Muntrie Big Article The silver market was firm this morning due to speculative purchases and weak gold currencies. At the opening, the July futures price was 45.54-46.29, up 24 pounds from the previous close.

Exchange Rates

US-UK The London foreign exchange market was firm and active today, with the pound sterling price stronger against the US dollar, due to the weakness of the French franc and other gold currencies. The opening exchange rate for US-UK was four yuan, nine jiao, three fen, nine san qi wu, lower than the US-UK closing rate on Saturday by one er wu. The price then rose steadily, and before noon the price was four yuan, nine wei, six fen, er wu, up two fen, yi ba qi wu from Saturday. There was a slight reaction at one o'clock in the afternoon, and the price fell back one er wu, to four yuan, nine jiao, six fen, yi er wu.

Securities

New York This morning, the stock market saw large-scale selling due to the unstable political situation in France and the continued weakness of the franc price. At the opening, the prices of various stocks fell sharply, with copper mines, railroads, automobiles, and steel stocks being the worst. Some fell by around one to three pounds. After a few minutes, the market price stabilized slightly, as trading conditions continued to improve, triggering new speculative buying. By 11:30 AM, the market had a strong reaction, recovering much of the previous decline. Major securities such as copper mines, steel, utilities, and railroads were down from one to one and a half pounds from the Saturday close. The New York stock market prices are listed on the left,
