All Sectors of Lancang, Yunnan Province, Strive for the Yunnan-Myanmar Border Line

Visiting Boundary Survey Committee to State Opinions

Striving on the Basis of Reason to Maintain National Territory

And Pointing Out Various Conspiracies Pre-Plotted by the British

Kunming Correspondence, The Yunnan-Myanmar boundary survey has been pending for a long time. In recent years, due to many national affairs, border affairs have been abandoned, and the British have taken the opportunity to operate, resulting in frequent border police reports. Since the central government appointed boundary survey personnel last year to go to Yunnan with British and neutral members to conduct on-site surveys on the border, the Chinese people have focused their attention. According to news from Lancang, this boundary survey is closely related to the survival of the county's borders. The gentlemen of the county specially convened a mass meeting to discuss ways to strive for the boundary. They elected Zhang Shi'an, the seventh district chief of the county, as well as Gong Zhiyi, Huang Daoneng, and Shi Youwen as representatives to visit the survey committee and express public opinion. The representatives believe that the matter concerns the country's borders, and that the area is the place that the British must contend for. Therefore, they have hurried off yesterday and have formulated two key points for striving before their departure, asking all parties to support and respond to preserve sovereignty. At the same time, they disclosed various conspiracies and designs pre-plotted by the British during the past boundary surveys. The key points and the British conspiracy are excerpted as follows:

Key Points for Striving

Please take the Nan Kong River as the natural boundary line between Yunnan and Myanmar. The reason is that Myanmar has historically been a vassal state of China. It was seized by the British by force in the eleventh year of Emperor Guangxu of the Qing Dynasty. Outside the territory of Myanmar, the area east of the Gunlong River has followed our orders. British government orders have not yet been reached, and it is naturally our territory. The British have no reason to force the name "Unfinished Boundary" and have no reason to invade the central part of our county. In order to prevent problems before they occur and stop the British's insatiable ambitions, please take the Nan Kong River as the natural boundary line to protect the border and save sovereignty. The land of the 11 Zhaohua should be assigned to our country. The reason is that the land of the 11 Zhaohua has previously accepted our country's appointment and has seals that can be verified. It should be assigned to our country. If this decision is due to the permission of the Chinese members, allowing the British army to enter the country, using force and frightening, and using various means of money temptation, causing them to be at a loss, the Chinese members must be responsible for restoring it in the future if the land of the 11 Zhaohua is assigned to the British.

British Conspiracy

The British conspiracies and tricks in the Yunnan-Myanmar boundary affairs are too numerous to mention. During the Guangxu years of the Qing Dynasty, the British took the opportunity of the boundary survey to operate in the Yunnan border (Lancang) territory. They specialized in making various conspiracies and facilities on the highest mountain, such as the so-called "hitting the sun," "looking at the telescope," chopping down trees, burying stones, etc. The general public did not understand their intentions and thought it was not important. It was not until Yong Weirui's aggressive teaching of affairs that it aroused old memories and knew that the British were felling big trees and burying stones on the Gao Feng Guan and Kongming Mountains. The intention was to pre-bury marks to make evidence for future boundary cheating. For a time, driven by patriotic heart, they automatically dug everywhere, but because of the long years, the place where the British buried the stones earlier could not be recognized. Only one piece was found in the Luoshuidong place, on which the handwriting can still be seen. In addition, Sigede of Ximishan (i.e., Ximeng) also buried three places, and it is said that there are inscriptions. It was dug up once a few years ago, but it was not found. Although this situation cannot determine the other party's intention at that time, it is known that if the result of this boundary survey dispute is not satisfactory to the other party, it is difficult to guarantee that it will not be used as evidence for the boundary dispute. Therefore, we dare to reveal it here first, so that the authorities know the details and the people of the country know its intentions, so as not to be deceived by its conspiracy. Then it is not only the blessing of Lancang County, but also the happiness of Yunnan Province and the whole of China.

Recent Situation of Mining Exploration in Anxi

—Poor Results from a Recent Drilling Hole—

Xiamen Correspondence, The iron ore in Anxi Pantianzhen, Fujian Province, is well-known at the time. Last year, the Construction Department hired members of the Geological Survey of the Academia Sinica to come to Fujian to survey. They believed that the iron in Pantian was still good and estimated that the reserves were 30 million tons. Afterwards, the Japanese technicians of the Shanghai Institute of Natural Sciences were hired to inspect it, and the results were the same. However, the survey could not determine exactly what the iron quality was and how much the ore deposit was. Last winter, the Anxi Mining Exploration Team was organized, and the Construction Department established the "Anxi Iron Ore Exploration Project Office", appointing Zhao Xiujin as the director and hiring 17 Japanese technicians from the South Manchuria Railway Co., Ltd., including Soma Hideo, to be divided into four departments: mineral surveying, cone testing, harbor, and railway. Zhao led the team to work in Anxi. Mineral surveying is geological investigation, railway is surveying and exploring the railway from the iron mine to the seaport, and harbor is surveying and exploring the seaport at the end of land transportation. If the ore is mined, production must be transported by sea and land for export. It is also a plan for the whole process. Until April, the work of mineral surveying, railway and harbor has been completed. Zhen's land is a silver-lead mixture and has no mining value. However, Pantian is very good. The Japanese technicians have returned to their country one after another. There is still a cone testing department specializing in Pantian iron ore, which is the most important part of the project. A diamond cone mining machine was borrowed from the South Manchuria Railway Company to drill a 400-meter-deep hole under the ore bed to explore the amount of iron stored in it and the iron content of the ore sand. In March, a hole was drilled in Pantian. The iron content of the ore sand was 50%, which can be called a good ore, and the reserves were rumored to be 80 million tons, but according to Li Qishan, a technician of the Construction Department, it should be 30 million tons. Currently, there are still three Japanese technicians in Anxi who are drilling mines: Nagaya Haraketsu, Takabayashi Ketsuro, and Fukuyama. At the end of April, another hole was drilled, 600 feet deep. The test results were not good. The ore sand components were not iron, and there was a layer of sand every other layer. After this hole is completed, it is planned to drill a hole, which can be completed by the end of August this year. The purpose of mining exploration is to determine the quality and reserves of iron in order to determine whether it is worth mining. Because the mining railway and harbor equipment requires a capital of 30 million yuan, we must be cautious. (May 3)

Zheng Zhaoqing's Report on the Inspection of the Huai River Diversion Project

Beijing News, Zheng Zhaoqing of the Economic Commission previously followed Sun Ke to inspect the Huai River Diversion to the Sea Project. After finishing the matter, he returned to Beijing and reported the inspection process to the commission as follows:

(1) Inspection Itinerary

On the morning of April 25, he followed Sun, the standing committee member of the Economic Commission, from Beijing by train to Zhenjiang to cross the river to Yangzhou, changed to a small wheel and went along the canal to Shaobo to inspect the ship lock project, and then to Gaoyou to inspect the Gaoyou ship lock, and stayed overnight in the wheel. At 10:00 AM on April 26, he arrived at Huaiyin, and then went to Yangzhuang to inspect the movable dam project and the nearby Huaiyin ship lock. In the afternoon, he inspected the Honghu Dam and the Huaiyin section of the Huai River Diversion to the Sea Waterway Project, and stayed overnight in Huaiyin. On April 27, he originally planned to go from Huaiyin to inspect the Huaihe River North Water Diversion Project, but because of the heavy rain last night, the road was impassable, so he still passed through the waterway to Huaian Baoying to Yangzhou. On April 28, he passed through Zhenjiang from Yangzhou and arrived in Beijing at about 7:00 PM.

(2) Shaobo Ship Lock

The Shaobo Ship Lock is one of the Huai River Diversion projects, which is sponsored by the Huai River Diversion Committee. The project requires 600,000 yuan. It started in February of the 23rd year. Connecting the canal is an important north-south transportation route. In recent years, the water volume has been unbalanced. The maximum draft depth of passing ships is only more than one meter, and the load is less than 100 tons. The navigation is almost stopped when the water level drops in spring and winter. Therefore, in the Huai River Diversion plan, we first start by cleaning up the canal waterway. The cleaning method is to build a new-style ship lock in the canal to maintain the water depth and maintain year-round navigation. The first phase of the project starts from Congjiakou, Weishan Lake, Shandong, and ends at Sanjiangying into the river, a total of 130 kilometers, with five ship locks, namely Desheng Lock, Heding Lock, Liulaojian Lock, Huaiyin Lock, and Shaobo Lock. The ones that have been started are Liulaojian, Huaiyin, and Shaobo Locks. After completion, the minimum water depth of the canal is 2.5 meters, and ships with a draft of 2 meters can pass unimpeded. The annual transportation volume in the canal now does not exceed one million tons at most. After the waterway is cleaned up, it will inevitably gradually increase. The Shaobo Ship Lock is used to maintain the water level of the canal between Shaobo and Huaiyin. The maximum water level difference between the two ends of the lock is 7.7 meters. It is the first ship lock from the river into the canal, located west of Shaobo Town, Jiangdu. The lock chamber is 10 meters wide and 100 meters long. Each time, 15 ships of 30 tons, 10 ships of 40 tons, 8 ships of 60 tons, 6 ships of 100 tons, 4 ships of 300 tons, and 1 ship of 900 tons can pass. The lock gate is made of steel with a switch machine on the top. A water channel is also set up on both sides of the lock chamber. If the ship comes from the upstream, first release water from the water pipe into the lock to make the water surface of the lock chamber level with the upstream, and then open the upper gate. The ship enters the lock, and at the same time, the upstream ship waiting in the lock chamber can leave the lock. Then close the upper gate and discharge the water to make the water level of the lock chamber level with the downstream, and then open the lower gate. The downstream ship can leave the lock and sail down, and at the same time, the upstream ship can enter the lock, and then close the lower gate. In this way, it is repeated once. When the water level difference between the upstream and downstream is the largest, it takes at most one hour. Now all parts of the ship lock have been built, and the filling project on both sides of the lock chamber is being handled. It is expected to be completed by the end of June this year.

(3) Gaoyou Ship Lock

According to the Huai River Diversion Plan, after the ship locks are built along the canal, the gap in the west dam of the canal that originally connected with the lake must be blocked. Then the canal and the lakes of Gaoyou will inevitably be isolated. Therefore, a small ship lock is built near the Yuehe Port in Er Ma Bridge, west of Gaoyou City, for the passage of sailing boats between the canal and the Gaobin Lake. The lock chamber is 10 meters wide and 29 meters long. Steel sheet piles are used as vertical walls on both sides. The lock gate is single-leaf type and is opened and closed by gear machinery. It started in June of the 24th year and was fully completed in April of the 25th year. The total cost of the project is more than 67,000 yuan.

(4) Huaiyin Ship Lock

The Huaiyin Ship Lock is sponsored by the Huai River Diversion Committee. Because the terrain of the canal from Zhangfuhekou to Huaiyin is very different, it is not easy to maintain the benefit of year-round navigation. In the past, four stone locks, such as Huiji, were built in Huaiyin to provide restraints. The water level difference between the upper and lower reaches of the lock is huge. Usually, when sailing ships pass through the lock, they have to use manpower to turn the ropes and cables and wind them around the bow and stern to barely pass. During the flood season, the water level difference between the upper and lower reaches is even greater, and it is impossible to pass. The Huai River Diversion Plan will make the Inner Canal only for transportation and the supply of irrigation water in the future. Therefore, a ship lock is built in Huaiyin. This ship lock is a safe navigation mechanism with new-style double-channel gates. A new canal is opened straight from Zhongmatou to Yangzhuang. The ship lock is built in this canal, located about eight kilometers west of Huaiyin County. The maximum water level difference between the upper and lower reaches of the lock is 9.2 meters. The bottom width of the lock chamber is 10 meters and the length is 100 meters. Its function is that on the Middle Canal, it can maintain the water level below the Suqian Liulaojian, and on the Huai River, it can maintain the water level below Huaiyuan, Anhui. Ships with a draft of 1.1 meters can pass unimpeded all year round. There are five advantages in its design. The first is the safety of the navigation channel, which can avoid the risk of boats passing through the old lock. The second is the improvement of navigation, which can provide for the passage of large vessels. The third is to shorten the voyage. The fourth is to build the ship lock. The construction does not hinder the current situation of the canal traffic. The fifth is that the old lock can be reused. It only needs to be slightly transformed to control the amount of irrigation water. The total budget for the project is 750,000 yuan. It started in March of the 23rd year. Now all the buildings have been mostly completed and are in progress. Filling work is being carried out on both sides. It is expected that all the projects can be completed by the end of June this year.

(5) Huai River Diversion to the Sea Waterway Project

The Huai River Diversion to the Sea is part of the Huai River Diversion Plan. This project is sponsored by the Jiangsu Provincial Government. The route starts from Yangzhuang, Huaiyin, and passes through Xiba, Lianshui, Dianhu, Yuntiguan, Qitao to Taozikou into the sea, with a total length of 167 kilometers. From Yangzhuang to Qitao, it is all in the old channel of the Yellow River. Below Qitao, a new river is opened to reach Taozikou. The original plan was for the river bottom to be 120 meters wide, with a slope of one to two point five on both sides, and a distance of 350 meters between the two dikes. In the first phase of the project, the river bottom was excavated first, with a width of 35 meters. Because the excavated soil was too far away, the distance between the two dikes was reduced to 230 meters. After completion, the discharge volume can reach 500 cubic meters per second. The total excavation volume of earthwork is 71 million cubic meters. The final approved budget was originally more than 9.8 million yuan. Later, because the soil quality of the abandoned Yellow River was mostly flowing sand and the seepage water was very strong, the river bed became deeper, and it was more difficult for manual excavation. In order to take into account the engineering expenses, the entire river bed was excavated one and a half meters less, leaving it to be scoured by water and excavated by machines. Therefore, the entire budget was reduced to more than 8.8 million yuan. In addition to the 2.2 million yuan subsidized by the association, the rest was raised by the Jiangsu Provincial Government. It started in October of the 23rd year. Civil workers were recruited from twelve counties including Huaiyin, Siyang, Jiangdu, Taixian, Lianshui, Huaian, Gaoyou, Shiying, Yancheng, Xinghua, Dongtai, and Funing to engage in work. Last month, more than 200,000 workers arrived. The first phase of earthwork can be completed by the end of May this year.

(6) Yangzhuang Movable Dam

The Yangzhuang Movable Dam is located at the western end of the sea waterway. Its purpose is to control the amount of water entering the sea from Hongze Lake and adjust the water level of the canal to facilitate irrigation and navigation. The dam adopts the Stone-Nae lift type. There are five holes, each 10 meters wide and 6.6 meters high, so it should meet the current discharge of the sea waterway. The dam base, dam pier, and highway bridge are cast with reinforced concrete, and steel sheet piles are used as bank revetment to prepare for the expansion of the sea waterway in the future. The height of the dam bottom is 7 meters, and the highest water level upstream during the water storage period is 15 meters. The budget for the project is 500,000 yuan, which is sponsored by the Huai River Diversion Committee. It started in November of the 24th year. By February 10th of this year, all the earthwork had been rushed to completion. Now the base pile project is being done, and five tenths of the steel sheet wall has been completed, and four-fifths of the pile driving work has been completed. It is estimated that the entire project can be completed by the end of August this year.

(7) Honghu Embankment

Hongze Lake is located southwest of Huaiyin, with Gao and Shi lakes to its east. The Huai River, carrying waters from Henan and Anhui provinces, flows into it. During the late Han Dynasty, Chen Deng, the administrator of Guangling, greatly promoted water conservancy and first built the Gao Embankment, blocking its lower reaches to make it flow north into the sea, preventing flooding in over a thousand miles of Huainan. Later generations of water managers all adhered to this old system without change. Since the Tang Dynasty, north-south transportation was open. By the Song Dynasty, the Yellow River shifted south, and the lake became wider and larger, forming a vast expanse of water. The importance of this embankment increased. During the Qingli reign of the Ming Dynasty, it was first repaired by Zhang Lunming, the transport commissioner, and then by Chen Xuan, the Earl of Pingjiang. During the Wanli reign, Pan Jixun, the director-general of river management, extensively repaired it, and reinforced over three thousand zhang with stone, making it even more solid. After the Yellow River flowed backward, the lakebed rose, and the lake water also rose accordingly. The terrain outside the embankment was low-lying. Once it breached, the seven counties downstream would become like the sea. In the Qing Dynasty, Jin Fu also greatly repaired and managed it. In the late Qing Dynasty, the Yellow River shifted north, and the Huai River lost its original course. The Huai River pooled in Honghu Lake, making the embankment even more important. From Huaiyin to Jiangba, the embankment is one hundred and twenty li long, remaining intact for hundreds of years. The Huai River Diversion Plan includes building an active dam at Jiangba to regulate the lake water. The dam is estimated to cost over five million yuan, and preparations for construction have already begun.

A Glimpse of Absurd Rumors in Fuzhou

Children Unexpectedly Suffer False Alarm

Almost All Elementary Schools in the City Suspend Classes

The Situation Calms Down After the Public Security Bureau Investigates and Bans the Rumors

Fuzhou Dispatch: At 10 a.m. on the 1st of this month, while elementary schools throughout the city were in session, rumors suddenly spread that the government intended to conscript children to go to Nangang to work on building dams, as practice for military service labor. It was also rumored that the construction of the Luoxing Pagoda wharf in Mawei by the Construction Bureau had been completed and required the blood sacrifice of seven boys and seven girls to prevent ships from colliding with the wharf in the future. It was further rumored that a white-knife fish spirit had been discovered in the Wulong River the day before, causing waves and obstructing ships from crossing the river. It had appeared in a dream to village elders, demanding the sacrifice of children before it would sink back into the river. Additionally, it was rumored that the Yellow River project in Shandong could not be completed and required five hundred children to fill the riverbed before the project could be finished, ordering each province to select twenty bright and intelligent children to be sent for use. Therefore, government officials were sending people to intercept homeless children on the streets. All of these were bizarre, preposterous, and unfounded rumors. Some even claimed that over a hundred children had already been taken from various elementary schools and loaded onto two public buses, to be transported along the Fuquan Highway and Fuma Highway. It was said with such vividness that many people without common sense or reason actually believed it to be true. In the morning, the rumors only circulated in Nantai, but by the afternoon, they had spread throughout the city. For a time, the city was in turmoil, and the people were alarmed. Children attending elementary schools felt as if a great calamity was imminent, and they rushed to be picked up. Many people gathered outside the gates of various elementary schools, clamoring and shouting, with the sounds of calling for sons and daughters filling the air. On the roads, women and men could be seen carrying children, sitting in vehicles, rushing back and forth, all with panicked expressions. The rickshaw business suddenly boomed. Even educated people, knowing that the above rumors were ridiculous, were bewildered by the state of the city. Fearing that some unexpected accident might have occurred, they also kept their children at home to ensure their safety. As a result, almost all elementary schools in the city suspended classes in the afternoon. Upon hearing the news, the Public Security Bureau, in addition to urgently ordering all branch bureaus and detective teams to investigate and arrest the rumor-mongers for prosecution, also dispatched police to various elementary schools to explain to the students' families that nothing was happening and to reassure them to return home. At the same time, it issued a notice strictly prohibiting rumors. The disturbance gradually subsided by night, and people began to calm down. As for the origin of these rumors, it is said that there were three possibilities. First, because the Public Security Bureau had decided to implement the crackdown on unregistered tutors from May 1st, it sent police to unregistered private schools, ordering them to disband. The students, suddenly seeing the police arriving, suspected that they were being arrested and fled in panic, causing a misunderstanding in the community. Another possibility was that because several incidents of children being run over by cars had occurred recently, the Public Security Bureau specially dispatched two public buses to patrol the city, picking up children wandering on the streets without adult supervision and taking them to the bureau to identify their families, notify them to come to the bureau, reprimand them, and have them take the children home. A third possibility was that students from a certain elementary school were traveling to Gushan for an excursion, riding together in a public bus. A soldier was sitting in the front of the bus. Passersby, seeing this, mistakenly believed that the elementary school students were being escorted by soldiers to work, thus fabricating this great mistake. However, investigations by the Public Security Bureau and various schools have shown that none of these actions had occurred. Therefore, where did the rumors actually come from? It is truly difficult to fathom. (May 2nd)

Songjiang: Completion of the Dredging of Panlong Pond

The Panlong Pond River is a waterway connecting Baiwo Township in the First District to Sijing in the Second District. It had not been dredged for a long time, gradually becoming silted up, causing the crops in the farmlands along the river to be poor in recent years. After the farmers in the area repeatedly requested dredging, it was approved by the county government, which appointed Chen Liuzhang as the director in charge of the dredging. It is now learned that the project was completed on April 29th and has been reported to the First District Office, requesting that it be forwarded to the county government to dispatch personnel for inspection and acceptance.

Suzhou: Unfavorable Weather Affects Silk Production

Due to weather conditions, the silkworm season in Suzhou is developing later than usual. The townships of Mudu, Xiangshan, the East and West Mountains of Dongting, and Hengjing are areas in Wu County that produce cocoons. The large silkworm farms have already begun feeding the silkworms leaves for three or four days, but because the weather is unevenly cold and warm, the success of hatching the silkworms is not good. In general, silkworm farmers are extremely worried. As for the issue of cocoon markets, the cocoon merchants who have applied for registration with the Agricultural Improvement District have reached thirty-five, including Gongda and Gongxin. Xiangshan and Dongshan have the most. The instructors of the Improvement District have already set out yesterday to provide guidance.

Film Actor Hong Ji Regains Freedom

The Shanghai Guangyi Film Company previously sent a large group of actors to Suzhou to shoot the film "Wang Shi Chuan." Because they had not applied to the Central Film Censorship Committee for review and approval, the Censorship Committee discovered this and sent Inspector Li Gongge and others to Suzhou, confiscating three thousand feet of the "Wang Shi Chuan" film that had not yet been completed. Wang Weiqing, the person in charge, was temporarily detained by the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau, and Hong Ji, the film's director, was taken to Beijing. The details of the incident have been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the Central Film Censorship Committee has thoroughly reviewed the film and determined that it does not contain any supernatural elements, and has released Hong Ji. Hong has returned to Suzhou. Wang Weiqing, who was temporarily detained by the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau, was also released on bail the other day. It is expected that the "Wang Shi Chuan" film will be returned soon and filming can continue.

Wuxi: Entire Village in Tuli Lane Burned Down

The home of Tu Fuxing, a resident of Tuli Lane in the northern countryside, suddenly caught fire on the evening of the other day, spreading to the homes of thirteen neighbors, including Tu Genpan, Tu Meisheng, and Li Apan. From east to west, everything was reduced to ashes. The men and women of the entire village cried to the heavens, and the sounds of weeping shook the sky. The scene was especially tragic. After investigation, it was found that a water buffalo was burned to death in Li Apan's house, and a five-year-old boy was burned to death in Tu Fuxing's house. A total of over fifty houses were burned down, with enormous losses. As for the cause of the fire, it is said that it was caused by a fox spirit.

Nantong: Security Expenses Centralized in Provincial Treasury

The security expenses of all counties in Jiangsu Province are now being uniformly collected and disbursed by the Management Office established by the District Security Command. Starting from the new fiscal year, the expenses of the security teams will be centralized in the provincial treasury. The district offices will soon be closing down. It is said that the reorganization of the security teams into regional groups will also be implemented at the same time.

Gaoyou: Septuagenarian Killed by Bandits

Zhu Zhaozheng, a farmer in Nanzhuang, Xi'an Township, Eighth District of this county, was seventy years old and from a family of modest means. At about 1 a.m. on the 28th, seven or eight bandits suddenly came, each carrying long and short guns, flashlights, and broadswords. They broke into the house, dragged Zhu out of bed, and burned his armpits with fire, demanding money. When they failed, they shot him in the lower abdomen, causing him to bleed profusely and lose consciousness. The bandits then looted the house and fled with the stolen goods. Neighbors, hearing the commotion, opened fire to chase after them. The bandits also returned fire, and the two sides engaged in a fierce battle for half an hour. The bandits were unable to withstand the pressure and fled.

Yangzhou: Villagers Gather to Fight Over Embankment, Injuring People

The Guadong river embankment in the Second District of Jiangdu is the most important guarantee for the farmlands and the lives of the people in the southeastern countryside. It has been designed and constructed by the Construction Bureau year after year, and it has been breached nine times. The other day, Wang Luozhang, the section chief of the Technology Section of the Construction Bureau, was sent to the embankment to survey the line and draw up plans, which were submitted for approval. One morning, Wang led five police officers from the Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau to the site, where they gathered workers who had already been hired and began construction according to the surveyed and determined embankment line. Unexpectedly, while Wang was giving instructions, villagers from outside the embankment forced him to retreat the embankment line, while villagers inside the embankment wanted to expand it outwards. Wang said that the line had been approved and could not be moved. This angered the villagers. Over a thousand men and women surrounded Wang, and eight or nine women grabbed Wang's arms while others punched and kicked him, forcing him to change the embankment line and hand over the drawings. Fortunately, Wang knew some martial arts and struggled to break free, running to the inside of the embankment. Then, they heard shouts of "Beat him to death" continuously. They chased him to the nearby Dragon King Temple, where he was already seriously injured, with a dizzy head. The villagers chased him to the temple and surrounded it again. Fortunately, Xiao Tongchun, a police officer from the local police station, pretended to invite "Committee Member Wang to the police station to answer the phone." Wang took the opportunity to leave the temple and promised to return the drawings. The crowd still chased after him, refusing to let him go. In this emergency situation, Yang Yuting, the patrol leader of the police station, led four police officers, hired a car to protect Wang, and rushed back to the bureau. It was already after 4 p.m. He reported the situation of the gathering crowd to the bureau chief, who in turn reported it to the county. He also learned that in addition to the embankment line, the villagers also demanded compensation for Qingyi farmland fees and digging fees. The government had never paid fees for digging and pressing farmland, and the green seedling fees had not been approved, so they were not accepted. It is now said that the county bureau is discussing solutions to the embankment line issue.

Court President Sworn into Office

Guo Wei, President of the Capital Court, held a swearing-in ceremony in the court's auditorium at 10 a.m. on the 3rd. Zhong Zhihan, Dean of the Fifth Branch of the Judicial Administration Department, was sent to preside over and witness the oath. Around a hundred people from the county's party and government organs, French officials, and representatives attended. After Chairman Zhong, the oath witness, led President Guo in taking the oath, the witness gave a speech, pointing out the need to eliminate outdated practices and implement psychological reconstruction. Next, Dai Tianqiu, President of the Jiangdu Lawyers Association, and Yu Peiren, Standing Committee Member of the County Party Department, gave speeches. Finally, President Guo gave a reply, resolving to act in accordance with the instructions of the oath witness. At 12 p.m., the ceremony ended with a group photo.

Hangzhou: Wall Collapse at Night Kills Two

The divorce case between Wang Jihuan, a famous scholar in western Zhejiang, and film star Wang Hanlun, which lasted for two years, has finally been resolved. Recently, Wang moved to No. 4 Xiaomixiang on April 1st because the old residence at the Qianwang Temple was dilapidated. Unexpectedly, the back wall of the house, which had not been repaired for many years, suddenly collapsed at 9:30 p.m. on the 3rd of this month, crushing a wing room. Wang Jihuan's nine-year-old daughter, Wang Kang, six-year-old son, Wang Yi, maid Xu, and male servant Zhao Shou were sleeping inside. Wang had not slept due to illness. He immediately reported the incident to the police station, which dispatched workers to excavate the site and send the injured to Guangji Hospital for treatment. As a result, the two children died one after another due to severe injuries. The maid Xu suffered injuries to her head and cheeks but was not in danger.

Wuhu: Anhui Implements Bureau Reduction and Department Conversion

Local Tax Bureaus Abolished Across the Board

The province of Anhui has now implemented the reduction of bureaus and conversion to departments. There have been many reforms in education, finance, and other areas. In the financial sector, all local tax bureaus in the province were abolished on May 1st. Business tax bureaus will be established in counties with annual tax revenues of over 30,000 yuan. In counties with revenues between 10,000 and 30,000 yuan, collection offices will be organized, supervised by the county magistrate and the head of the relevant department. Counties with total provincial and county tax revenues of less than 10,000 yuan per year may apply to the provincial government for approval to have the relevant department establish tax collectors to handle the work directly. All newly converted business tax bureau counties also began operations on May 1st. The grades and expenses are as follows: Grade A: Xuan City, Hefei, Hexian, Wuwei, Dangtu, Fuyang, and Huoqiu. Grade B: Huaining, Hao County, Su County, Shou County, Nanling, and Tongcheng. Grade C: Wuhu, Fengyang, Xiuning, Si County, Tongling, Guoyang, Shucheng, Dingyuan, Jing County, Yingshang, Chao County, Tianchang, Mengcheng, She County, Chuzhou, Huaiyuan, Wuhe, Lujiang. The total monthly expenses are 4,320 yuan, and the annual budget is 51,840 yuan. Counties that have not established business tax bureaus but have established tax collection offices include Susong, Taihu, Guangde, Taihe, Quanjiao, Hanshan, Qingyang, Fanchang, Langxi, Lu'an, Ningguo, Fengtai, Wangjiang, Dongliu, Huoshan, Zhide, Huoqiu, Xuyi, Linquan, Dangshan, Jiashan, Qimen, Huoxian, Jixi, Jingde, Taiping, Shidai, Wuhe, and Lihuang. The total monthly expenses are 1,772 yuan, and the annual budget is 29,264 yuan. All are now collecting taxes according to the standards set by the Department of Finance.

Xiaoshan: Kancun Fanjiayuan Becomes a Marsh

The farmland in Fanjiayuan, Jiangbin Township, Kancun County, Xiaoshan, covers over two thousand mu. Due to continuous rain in recent days, the accumulated water is over a foot deep, turning the area into a vast expanse of water. Because it is surrounded by the new sand dike, there is no way for the water to drain out. If the submergence lasts too long, the spring crops will be completely destroyed. Yesterday (the 2nd), the farmers in the area gathered and requested that Yang Peinan, the director of the Zhangshendian Farmers Association, help them find a way to open the dike. Mr. Yang, along with Mr. Wang of the Nansha Water Conservancy Association, went to the site to inspect it. They found that the dike was indeed hindering the farmland irrigation. As the matter concerned agricultural production, it was proposed to open the dike immediately for rescue, and at the same time, prepare to build a sluice gate for irrigation and drainage of the accumulated water.

Local News

Dr. Wang Chonghui Scheduled to Go to Beijing This Week to Meet Chiang

Wei Daoming and Cheng Tiangu Will Accompany Him

May Travel South Around the 20th to Welcome Hu

Shanghai Times News: Central Committee Member Dr. Wang Chonghui decided to go to Beijing, but after returning to Shanghai, he suffered from severe nasal and dental ailments. Therefore, he has rarely left his residence in Shanghai, except to seek medical treatment and meet with various important figures to discuss the draft constitution, in order to avoid fatigue. It is now learned that Wang's ailments have been cured, and he will wait for President Chiang to return to Beijing before meeting with him. Then, around the 20th of this month, he will travel to Guangdong with President Dai, Vice President Xu, and others to welcome Hu Hanmin north. The details are as follows:

Going to Beijing This Week

Wang decided to go to Beijing to meet with President Chiang and various important figures of the Central Committee. Spring Cocoon Loan Syndicate to Hold Joint Meeting Today

Nineteen Silver and Money Firms Have Joined

Loans Expected to Be Released Around the 20th

Nineteen silver and money firms in this city have jointly formed the Spring Cocoon Loan Syndicate for the 25th year. The syndicate has drafted various rules and regulations and will submit them for approval at a general meeting on the 5th. It will then proceed with its organization. Loans are expected to be released around the 20th. The details are as follows:

Meeting Today

The Spring Cocoon Loan Syndicate was initiated by the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and other banks. To date, eighteen banks and one money shop have joined. However, the syndicate still hopes for the cooperation of the silver and money industry. At the syndicate's inaugural meeting, various principles were formulated, and seven banks, including the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, were selected to draft the organizational charter, loan regulations, and detailed rules of procedure. A joint meeting will be held at the Bank of Communications on the Bund at 3 p.m. today to discuss the progress. It will then proceed with organizing the office.

Transferring Personnel for Office Work

The syndicate is a short-term organization, so the internal personnel will be temporarily transferred from the participating banks. The syndicate will appoint five standing committee members to handle important business. The office will be located in Shanghai and will have two divisions: general affairs and accounting. Each division will have a director and several staff members. The general affairs division will be responsible for documents, investigation, and other matters, and the accounting division will be responsible for calculation, auditing, and other matters. Branch offices will be established in Hangzhou and Wuxi to handle investigation and loan matters in the vicinity.

Scheduled Loan Release

It is said that the interest rate on the syndicate's loans is very low, but the procedures for investigating applicants and supervising cocoon collection are cautious and strict. After manufacturers apply for registration, the investigation is verified, and the amount of the loan is approved, the applicant is notified to contact the office with 30% of the guarantee money. The syndicate will send personnel with the money to collect the cocoons. The collected cocoons will be stored in a warehouse designated by the syndicate. If there is no syndicate bank warehouse nearby that can be used, the cocoons will be stored in the factory and supervised by syndicate personnel. It is said that cocoon registration in Zhejiang Province has already been completed, so loans can be released around the 20th, once the office is established.

After another round of consultations, there should be no problems.

Qian Reports on Petitioning Process

The China General Chamber of Industry and the National Federation of Commerce sent Qian Chengxu to Anhui to petition regarding the Anhui Province's monopoly on Qihong tea. Qian arrived in Anqing on the 29th of last month. At that time, he mediated between the opinions of Anhui Province on the monopoly of black tea and the Shanghai tea houses and suggested to the provincial government. After several consultations, an agreement was reached on the second day. The provincial government expressed acceptance of Qian's proposal for official-merchant cooperation and the establishment of a Chinese tea management organization and proposed three counter-proposals as the basis for future agreements. Qian took the Jianghua ship east on the third day, first to Nanjing, to present the mediation process to the Ministry of Industry, and then returned to Shanghai to report on it when the Ministry's attitude was determined.

Suggestions to Provincial Government Actually See Original Text

The original text of Qian Chengxu's suggestion is as follows: "As a representative of the China General Chamber of Industry and the National Federation of Commerce, I have come to your province to offer mediation on the issue of suspended exchange by Shanghai tea houses. My sole purpose is to exert a lateral force to break the deadlock and prevent the conflict from escalating and affecting tea-growing regions in other provinces. I also deeply feel that a national economic organization is a collection of multiple parts, breathing in unison for a healthy body. Regarding the issue of your province's control of tea production, I believe that improving quality, aiding farmers, and unifying production and sales are necessary. However, there are several processes in the commercial sector that must temporarily pass through merchants as a transition to achieve the direct goal of production and sales. I am also concerned about the impact on Chinese tea exports this year. For the benefit of both parties, I suggest that your government continue to advance the established tea production and marketing organization according to the original plan. For foreign trade, the existing tea houses should be reorganized into Chinese tea management organizations under the supervision and guidance of the government. I consulted the Ministry of Industry on this and they found it appropriate and feasible. The Ministry has already telegraphed your provincial government for verification. My opinions are listed below. Tea house merchants are more suitable for promotion due to their experience and past foreign trade relations. I propose that officials and merchants jointly establish a Chinese tea business company with a fixed capital of 3 million yuan, with merchants investing 2 million yuan and the government 1 million yuan. The company's business includes purchasing tea leaves and promoting sales at home and abroad. A general management office should be established above the company, using a committee system with five to seven members as the chairman of the committee. The general manager of the company shall be selected by the committee from the merchant shareholders (i.e., non-merchant shareholders shall not serve as general manager). In the current situation, the Qimen black tea under the control of your provincial government has resulted in the simultaneous suspension of green tea exchange. Your provincial government has its own views on the future development and handling of the situation, which I will not express. However, as a suggestion, if your provincial government intends to accept the above principles, I will do my best to mediate and promote its realization and resolve the issue of tea merchants suspending exchange." The Anhui Provincial Government added three principles to Qian's proposal, including: "If the Ministry of Industry has an overall plan for the Chinese tea trading company and is responsible for it, our province will accept it. Our province's handling of black tea marketing this year only aims to reduce loan interest rates, reduce tea tax rates, eliminate the tea houses' past bad practices towards tea companies, and seek convenience and safety in transportation. Further improvements will be made to rationalize production and sales. Regarding the tea houses' suspension of green tea loans, Director Zhao Lanping of the National Economic Commission is responsible for mediation. If the suspension continues after May 5, our province will seek other relief measures."

Head of the German Economic Investigation Mission, Dr. Krup, Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

I Admit to Having Signed the German-Puppet Commerce Agreement

Said It Was Just an Informal Commercial Instrument

Dr. Krup, the head of the German Far East Economic Investigation Mission, came to China again from Japan and arrived in Shanghai on the President Monroe wheel of the Da Lai Company at 3:00 PM yesterday. Mr. Krup admitted that he had signed the so-called "German-Puppet Commerce Agreement." The following are the details of his arrival in Shanghai and his speech:

Arrival in Shanghai

The wheel was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 2:00 PM, but it was delayed until 3:00 PM. It berthed at the Da Lai Pier in Bailianjing, Pudong. Mr. Krup's decision to come to China from Japan was very secret, and even his wife did not come with him. His name was not listed in the passenger list of the President Monroe wheel. The reporter from Xinsheng News Agency searched everywhere without success. Later, he met Ge Linfu, the president of the German News Agency, who came to meet him, and he was introduced to meet him. After getting off the wheel, Mr. Krup changed to a small passenger wheel to cross the Pu, and landed at the New Customs Pier at 4:00 PM. He first went to the German Consulate on Huangpu Road to rest. Mr. Krup's visit here will last a considerable amount of time, and he will go to Beijing to pay respects to our authorities to explain everything. The rumor that Mr. Krup will take the original wheel back to Europe this morning is untrue.

Krup's Speech

According to Mr. Krup, who spoke to reporters on the wheel, the report that I signed the "German-Puppet Commerce Agreement" in Japan is not true. The report is probably a mistake of an informal commercial arrangement, not any agreement or article. This is all about the exchange rate relationship and has no political meaning. There is no suspicion of recognizing the puppet Manchukuo, and I am not a government official in active service. I have been out of the official circle for three years. This decision is only to serve as the head of the Far East Economic Investigation Mission in my private capacity, in order to promote the trade relationship between Germany and the Far East. After arriving in Shanghai, it is still uncertain how long he will stay in Shanghai and when he will go to Beijing. In the future, he will return to his country via Siam, but the trip is also undecided.

Page 10

Due to Smuggling and Other Relations, Nanhua Shipping Declines Sharply

Smuggled Sugar Floods, Domestic Sugar Becomes Stagnant

Currency Value Differences, Commerce Depressed

Minnan Shipping Becomes Abnormal, Japanese Ships Increase Uniquely

Nanhua's shipping between Shantou, Hong Kong, Guangdong, Fujian, and other ports has always been very prosperous. In the past two months, the situation has changed drastically and has declined sharply. The fundamental main reason is the flooding of smuggled goods in North China, which has affected freight in South China. Shipping lines in Shanghai, both Chinese and foreign, have suffered major blows. The detailed details of this matter are described as follows:

Smuggled Sugar Affects Domestic Sugar

Guangdong sugar sells well in Shanghai and also sells to ports along the Yangtze River. Because it is tax-free when imported, it is cheaper than foreign sugar. Therefore, Guangdong sugar has occupied a very large force in Shanghai. Four factories in Guangdong are rushing to produce it, and large quantities are shipped from Shantou to Shanghai. In the past two months, due to smuggling in North China, tax-free sugar has been sold privately to Shanghai and ports along the Yangtze River. According to the investigation results, the price of smuggled sugar is below 14 yuan per dan. Guangdong sugar was first sold for 21 yuan, then fell to 19 yuan, and recently decreased by 2 yuan, but it is still not as cheap as smuggled sugar. As a result, Guangdong sugar arrives in Shanghai and is piled up in countless quantities. The China Merchants Bureau alone transports it, and the sugar piled up in the southern warehouse is already difficult to accommodate. In the past half month, Guangdong sugar shipped from Shantou has been changed to unloading in the northern warehouse. The more storage, the more backlog, and the more stagnant the sales. In the past week, Guangdong has implemented a reduction in sugar shipped to Shanghai. Moreover, due to the fundamental impact of smuggling on sales, the number of shipments in North China and Central China has fallen sharply. Therefore, two factories have stopped. Starting from the end of this month, Guangdong sugar will temporarily stop being shipped to Shanghai.

Currency System Changes Commerce

Guangdong used to use Hao Yang as the unit. The purchase of Shanghai goods has always been calculated in cooperation with the Shanghai ocean according to the Hao Yang market price, roughly increasing by more than 20% according to the declared price. Now Guangdong Province is also following the central government's new system to reform the circulating Hao Yang and adopt the legal currency system. During this transition period, the exchange rate between Shanghai and Guangdong has invisibly changed in a new way. One yuan of Shanghai legal currency is worth 1.5 yuan of Guangdong legal currency. Due to the transformation of the currency system, the transportation of goods from Shanghai to Guangdong must be invisibly increased by 25% compared with the previous one. However, although the cost is high, it is still difficult to increase the price after being sold in Guangdong. The Guangdong gang is concerned about the blood capital, and except for the necessary goods that have to be considered for handling, other goods (Shanghai's goods transported to Guangdong include yarn cloth, textiles, cigarettes, grains, sundries, and foreign sundries) are all holding a wait-and-see attitude, resulting in a sudden sharp decline in the number of goods transported from Shanghai to Shantou, Xiamen, and Guangdong, a decrease of almost 40%. Nanhua's shipping industry of various Chinese and foreign shipping companies in Shanghai has been severely affected. Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, and others still have a part of transshipment goods. The China Merchants Bureau's Nanhua liner due to poor business in this way, only four new liners were changed to one flight per week, and four to five fewer flights per month. This is also a major depression in the shipping industry.

Shanghai-Fujian Wheel Also Lacks Energy

Although the Minnan Construction Department has dredged Hanjiang this year, and Nantai can pass seagoing vessels, the Shanghai-Fuzhou route has also declined because Japanese goods sell well and domestic goods in Fujian are suppressed, and the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway is open to traffic. , the goods transported to the border between Minnan and Jiangxi are transported by car, resulting in a decline in the number of goods loaded from Shanghai into Fuzhou. The new inscriptions of the China Merchants' Shanghai-Fujian wheel have been changed to sail in Beiyang, and the Wanhong of Sanbei has been changed to sail in the Yangtze River. The Jing'an wheel traveling between Shanghai and Fujian can only load 20% to 30% of its feet. During this depression, the number of Japanese ships sailing from Shanghai to Fuzhou has increased from three to six. It is not difficult to find out the reason.

Traces of Contemporaries

Kong Xianxi, Zou Lin, Liu Ruiheng, Zeng Rongfu, and Liu Weichi took the overnight train from Shanghai to Beijing last night.

Telephone Meeting to Regularly Convene Various Groups: Joint Telephone Conference

Discussing Sound Organization to Seek Vigorous Resistance

Recommending Proper Methods to Write to Chinese Directors for Negotiation

The Special District Telephone Problem Committee of this city, in order to enrich its organization and resolutely resist the new telephone system, has decided to convene a joint conference of various influential public groups in the concession area on the eighth of this month at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to discuss methods. The committee also sent a letter to the Chinese directors attending the Municipal Council yesterday, requesting them to raise serious concerns with the Municipal Council. The details are recorded below:

Regularly Scheduled Meetings to Discuss Methods

The Special District Telephone Problem Committee yesterday sent a letter to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Concession, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the First and Second Special District Citizens' Federation, the Bankers' Association, the Lawyers' Association, the Joint Association of Brokers of the Five Exchanges, and the Guangdong, Ningbo, Pudong, and other fellow-provincial associations, stating: "Since the implementation of the new special district telephone system, users in various districts have risen up in protest. At a time when the market is declining and commerce is sluggish, we are already feeling the hardship of 'living in Shanghai is not easy.' How can we bear to add an unexpected burden on top of tightening our belts and勉維殘局 (struggling to maintain the remaining situation)? Upon investigation, the Shanghai Telephone Company, disregarding social economics, has even been found to have inflated the final account. If we do not deal with it, then in the future, everything for us citizens of the special district will be at its disposal. The crisis ahead is unimaginable. In order to strive permanently and seek a solution, we have decided to convene a joint conference of various groups in the special district at 3:00 PM on Friday, the eighth of this month, at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce in Tianhou Palace Bridge, to discuss a unified stance. We are specially writing to your association, requesting you to send two representatives to attend and participate in the discussion. The committee also notified all executive committee members and advisors to attend and discuss coping methods."

Letter to Chinese Directors Requesting Negotiation

Yesterday, a letter was also sent to the Chinese directors of the Municipal Council, Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu, Jiang Yiping, Guo Shun, Xi Yushu, etc., stating: "The Shanghai Telephone Company, in order to satisfy its desire for a one-tenth official profit, has specially formulated new rules, which have been implemented since March 1 of this year. The fees are charged according to the number of calls made. Users throughout the city have repeatedly protested against this disguised price increase, but to no avail. Recently, users from various districts have reported to the committee that the company has inflated the final account and charged unexpected fees. Such unethical behavior is not allowed by law, reason, or human sentiment. In order to avoid being unreasonably victimized, users from various districts have risen up to refuse payment and allow their lines to be cut. Their loyalty and courage for the public good are commendable. However, Shanghai is a mixed Chinese and foreign city, and an important commercial port. If transportation is restricted, the future of commerce will be difficult to develop. Furthermore, in the event of fires, burglaries, or ambulance services, it will be impossible to transmit messages in a timely manner. We are specially writing to request your directors to prioritize the protection of the interests of the Chinese people and promptly raise serious concerns with the Municipal Council, and demand that:　The basic call allowance should be abolished, and all calls should be charged at a rate of three cents per call;　Residential telephones should have a minimum monthly usage of six yuan and fifty cents; Commercial telephones should have a minimum monthly usage of ten yuan; Each telephone should be equipped with a meter to ensure credibility; If the company's net profit exceeds ten percent, the price should be reduced immediately; If the company still cannot accept the above minimum requirements, the Municipal Council should immediately cancel its business license and solicit new investors, or the state should estimate and purchase it. We believe that all directors, entrusted with the heavy responsibility of the city's taxpayers, will be able to uphold public opinion and work hard to negotiate, thus satisfying the public's expectations."

The entire New Life Movement General Association inspection team, numbering over one hundred, went to the Municipal Government at 10:00 AM yesterday to participate in the Premier's Commemoration Week. Mayor Wu led the ceremony, and Jiang Juehua, the section chief of the Second Section of the Municipal Public Works Bureau, reported on his inspection of highways in Europe and the United States. The gist was that highways in Europe and the United States have developed extremely rapidly, and their construction is also very sophisticated, especially in England. However, the construction projects in England, the United States, and other countries are extremely sophisticated and costly, and are not very suitable for China. The projects in France and Germany are economical, and the effectiveness is considerable, which is enough for our country's method. There are still technical aspects, but due to time constraints, they have not been reported. The meeting adjourned at 11:00 AM. Mayor Wu led a tour of the various bureaus under the Municipal Government, as well as the Municipal Library, Museum, and Sports Field. At 12:00 noon, Mayor Wu hosted a lunch for the team at the Municipal Government and invited the staff of the Municipal New Life Movement Association to accompany them. During the lunch, Mayor Wu gave a speech, stating that the New Life Movement is of utmost importance to the revival of our country. The promotion of the New Life Movement must be divided into two aspects, one focusing on the spirit, which can also be called education, and the other focusing on the material. He hopes that the New Life Movement General Association inspection team will openly criticize and guide the city's New Life Movement work, and also hopes that those responsible for the city's New Life Movement will not work nervously because the General Association inspection team is in Shanghai, nor will they slack off after the inspection team leaves Shanghai. Finally, Deputy Team Leader Liu gave a reply, stating that although Shanghai has been affected by the January 28 Incident and the environment is different from the interior, the achievements in material construction and the efforts to promote the New Life Movement are all admirable. This is all a manifestation of the local authorities' willingness to take responsibility. He hopes that they will continue to work hard for the revival of the nation. The guests and hosts parted happily at 1:00 PM. In addition, over fifty inspectors stationed by the New Life Movement inspection team in various public security agencies to assist in promoting the New Life Movement have now concluded their work and have all withdrawn yesterday. The inspectors are currently drafting reports. Furthermore, since the team arrived in Shanghai, they have been working hard every day. Therefore, today is a holiday in commemoration of Premier Sun Yat-sen's inauguration as the Extraordinary President, and the inspectors will be free to visit Wusong and other places.

Xiong Zhi Returned to China Yesterday, Talking About Child Welfare in Europe, America, and China

All Countries Pay Great Attention to Child Welfare

Complete Facilities Can Be Modeled After Us

Ms. Xiong Zhi, a foreign inspector of the China Child Welfare Association, went abroad last September to inspect child welfare in various countries. After spending more than eight months in Europe and America, she has now completed her work and returned to Shanghai at 11:30 AM yesterday. The ship docked at the Gonghexiang Wharf. Chen Tiesheng, Chen Zhengfan, and Xiong Xiling, etc., the Director-General and staff of the China Child Welfare Association, all went to the wharf to welcome her. After disembarking, Ms. Xiong returned to her residence on Lafayette Road to rest. A reporter from the Shenshi News Agency made a special visit to interview her, and she shared her observations on child welfare in Europe and America, which are recorded below. The China Child Welfare Association, in view of the rapid progress of child welfare in various countries and her own interest in child welfare, sent her to various countries for inspection on September 7 last year. She visited England, Italy, the United States, Germany, France, Russia, and other countries, and the facilities for child welfare can be divided as follows: Italy: She stayed in Italy for two months, visiting more than ten cities and visiting the Italian Mother and Child Protection Association, etc. Under the rule of Mussolini, Italy pays great attention to child welfare. General associations are set up in various cities, and branches are set up in rural areas, which are very common. United States, France, and England: The child welfare associations in these three countries are mostly funded by public fundraising. Children under the compulsory education age of seven are educated by nurseries, infant schools, and early childhood welfare associations, but there are also slight differences. Nurseries specialize in caring for infants under two years old, infant schools care for children aged two to four, and early childhood welfare associations care for children under seven years old. Russia: Child welfare in Russia is very developed because the government has assisted it with state power, so the results are particularly remarkable. Germany seems to be following Russia's trend. In short, she observed that all European and American countries attach great importance to the welfare of children and regard children as the future masters of the country. To seek the prosperity of the nation, we must first seek the welfare of children and provide them with appropriate education. She is currently sorting out materials and reporting to the China Child Welfare Association, and will bring back many new educational tools and toys for children for public exhibition, as a reference for improving China's emerging child welfare.

Reorganization of Salt Affairs Agencies in Lianghuai

Huaihe and Huaibei Areas Merged into Lianghuai Area

Deputy Salt Transport Commissioner of Huainan Abolished, Salt Transport Commissioner Still Stationed in Guanyun

In order to reorganize salt affairs in Huaihe, the Ministry of Finance has decided to merge Huaihe and Huaibei into the Lianghuai area. The Salt Transport Commissioner of Lianghuai will still be stationed in Guanyun, the Deputy Salt Transport Commissioner of Huainan will be abolished, and the Huaibei Salt Affairs Audit Branch will be renamed the Lianghuai Salt Affairs Audit Branch, with Yao Yuanlun, the current manager of the Huaibei Branch, serving as the manager of the Lianghuai Branch and concurrently as the Salt Transport Commissioner. The Yangzhou Accumulation Audit Branch will be reduced in scope and renamed a sub-branch, under the jurisdiction of the Lianghuai Branch, with Niu Jianxia as the director of the sub-branch. It is also heard that the salt sold in the four ports of Yangzi was originally supplied by the various fields in Huainan, and the Salt Transport Commissioner of Lianghuai was stationed in Jiangdu to preside over everything. Later, due to the eastward migration of the sea, the original salt kilns in Huainan were far from the sea, the salinity was weak, and the production was greatly reduced. In order to adjust supply and demand, new滩Huai salt production centers were added in Huaibei. The center of gravity shifted from south to north, and in 1931, the Salt Transport Commissioner of Lianghuai was moved to Guanyun. The original Deputy Salt Transport Commissioner of Huaibei was renamed the Deputy Salt Transport Commissioner of Huainan and moved to Jiangdu. Now, a further step has been taken to unite the salt administration of Lianghuai into one area.

Municipal Association Sends Letter to Municipal Council to Compensate for Those Killed by Stray Bullets

Because Most Pedestrian Streets are for the Working Class

Once a Family Member is Killed or Injured, the Family Loses its Support

The First Special District Citizens' Association sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "According to a letter from citizen Zhou Qifan, Chinese people seek refuge in the concession, believing it to be safe and reliable. However, in recent years, theft cases have occurred repeatedly, and stray bullets have injured and killed pedestrians, which is not uncommon. The danger is imminent, and life is at stake. Commentators say that this is caused by inaccurate shooting by detectives chasing bandits. Although shooting to apprehend bandits is necessary given the circumstances, injuring and killing passersby is also tolerated by law. However, those who are injured and killed by stray bullets are innocent victims. From a moral standpoint, even if it is difficult to appeal to the law, the Municipal Council of the Concession cannot sit idly by without providing appropriate compensation to the deceased and injured. Moreover, most pedestrian streets are for the working class who are directly involved in production. Once a family member is killed or injured, the family loses its support. Everyone has the same heart, how can this be tolerated? Furthermore, the Public Concession Municipal Council spends over ten million yuan a year as security expenses for the police, which is considerable. However, robbery cases occur repeatedly and are heard of daily. Bandits are as rampant as ever. If the tiger and rhinoceros escape from the cage and the tortoise and jade are destroyed in the coffin, whose fault is it? The concession is leased territory of our country, and most of the revenue comes from Chinese taxes. The weakness of security guarantees has reached this point. Since the Municipal Council does not hesitate to spend high salaries to support useless people, it should provide generous compensation to those who are innocently killed or injured by stray bullets during bandit hunts to comfort the families of the deceased and prevent them from freezing and starving. Human sentiment and law should be balanced. In addition to separately writing to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession to earnestly negotiate with the Municipal Council and request that in the event of the above situation, compensation should be determined according to the severity of the injury, we are correspondingly writing to your association to uphold justice and unanimously negotiate with the Municipal Council to achieve this goal. It is our duty to do so, and we hope that you will review and reply." The matter was submitted to the first joint meeting of the fifth session of the executive and supervisory committees for discussion, and it was believed that the above-mentioned matters were indeed true. Accordingly, a letter was sent to your bureau, requesting that compensation should be provided for those who are injured and killed by stray bullets during robbery cases, etc., in order to maintain human sentiment and fairness.

Ice Fresh Fish Industry Association Telegraphed Finance Minister Kong Requesting Correction of Fish Market Regulations

It is learned that the Ice Fresh Fish Industry Association of this city telegraphed Finance Minister Kong regarding the fish market regulations, stating: "To Minister Kong of the Nanjing Ministry of Finance, we humbly submit that yesterday's Shen Bao newspaper column revealed news of the Shanghai Fish Market Joint Stock Company, item B of the discussion and resolution items, stating that this association notified the Ministry of Finance that from the afternoon of May 10, fish cargo ships from all ports must all dock at the fish market for transactions, etc., and a letter was sent to the association, the matter being the same as before. The association convened an industry meeting at 1:00 PM on May 2, and unanimously agreed that the fish market and the fish firms are both intermediaries and should strictly abide by the boundaries and operate in their respective industries. Article 3 of the company's articles of association states that 'after the opening of this market, no business of the same or similar nature may be conducted within the Shanghai area.' However, the articles of association of a joint stock company cannot restrict the resolutions of third parties in the record. The fish market resolved that fish cargo ships from all ports must all dock at the fish market for transactions, which means detaining ships for delivery. However, detaining ships for delivery is the authority of the customs, which is applied to those who violate laws, evade taxes, or transport contraband. Now, the fish market does not know that it is a joint stock company and wants to use its own articles of association to bind the business of others. Therefore, there is a resolution to notify the Ministry of Finance. We are afraid that your department will be deceived by it and grant its request, which will cause difficulties for the members of the association and the fishermen. We must urgently present the reasons and telegraph to your lord for investigation. We humbly beg you to consider that our industry is facing difficulties under the attack of the economic downturn, and the situation is self-evident. The request of the Shanghai Fish Market to detain ships for delivery should be rejected, which is both in the public interest. Respectfully submitted, the Ice Fresh Fish Industry Association of Shanghai kowtows, winter."
