Educational News

Anglo-American Return of Boxer Indemnity Funds: The Situation of Educational and Cultural Development in China. The United States has already returned the funds twice, and the United Kingdom since 1922.

Since the United States first proposed returning a portion of the Boxer Indemnity to China in 1909, many have followed suit. The following is a summary of an investigation into the use of the Boxer Indemnity funds returned by the United Kingdom and the United States for educational and cultural development in China:

United States

Regarding the return of the Boxer Indemnity between China and the United States, there is a formal note from the Chinese Minister to the United States, Mr. Shi, to the U.S. Department of State, dated June 6, 1915, and a formal note from the U.S. Department of State to the Chinese Minister to the United States, dated July 20, along with the attached order from the U.S. President to implement the return of the Boxer Indemnity, as evidence. The Boxer Indemnity has been returned twice. The first return was implemented starting in January 1909, totaling USD 28,901,509.31, specifically for the establishment of Tsinghua Academy and sending students to study in the United States. The second return was USD 12,545,438.67, of which USD 6,131,755.09 was principal and USD 6,413,683.58 was interest, to be paid in 20 years. The fixed amount to be received annually is USD 539,588.76. The year the entire U.S. Boxer Indemnity will be fully paid off is expected to be 1946. The Sino-American institution managing the returned Boxer Indemnity jointly formed the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture, which was established in September 1924. It is an independent entity. The Chinese directors include Cai Yuanpei and ten others, and the American directors include John Leighton Stuart and five others. The foundation manages the allocation of the Boxer Indemnity. Apart from retaining a portion as a permanent fund, the remainder is used to subsidize educational and cultural endeavors, including: (1) Educational endeavors, tentatively focusing on scientific research (including physics, chemistry, biology, geology, and astronomy), scientific applications (including agriculture, engineering, and medicine), and science education (including science education and scientific research on education); cultural endeavors are tentatively limited to libraries; other educational and cultural endeavors with nationwide impact are also under consideration. When providing subsidies to a certain institution, in addition to requiring past achievements and the ability to maintain the status quo, an important condition is the ability to raise a portion of the funds themselves. Except for those receiving only a one-time subsidy, unless otherwise agreed or planned, annual subsidies are tentatively limited to three years. If there are no significant achievements during the subsidy period, the foundation may stop paying the subsidy at any time. Any requests for allocation of funds for use as a foundation will not be granted. The foundation's past endeavors have been detailed in the foundation's annual reports, and only the main points of the foundation's activities in the 24th year are described below. A. Self-managed activities: The number of science professorships established this year is six, three fewer than in the 23rd year. As of July of the 24th year, the schools and departments where professorships have been established include: Wuhan University, physics (established for six years), chemistry (established for six years), zoology (established for five years), and botany (established for six years); Sichuan University, zoology (established for five years) and educational psychology (established for six years). More than 50 people were awarded science research grants and subsidies after review. The Compilation and Translation Committee has achieved considerable success, with translated publications. B. Jointly managed activities include the National Peiping Library (the library was officially opened in June 1931 in cooperation with the Ministry of Education; this year, the library also exchanged librarians with the Bibliothèque nationale de France in Paris for the first time, with Mr. Wang Chongmin sent abroad and Ms. Nolleap coming to the library to work), the Jing Sheng Biological Research Institute (the institute was established in memory of Fan Jing Sheng, a former director of the foundation, with a fund of 150,000 yuan allocated by the Shangzhi Society and entrusted to the foundation to form the institute), the foundation's cooperative research fund with Peking University (the foundation and Peking University agreed to allocate 200,000 yuan each as a special fund for cooperative research; later, it was agreed that from the 23rd year to the 26th year, the foundation would allocate 109,000 yuan each year, while Peking University would still allocate 200,000 yuan; the purpose is to establish research professorships at Peking University, to supplement the equipment of Peking University's libraries, instruments, and other institutions, and to establish scholarships and grants for Peking University students; this year, there are a total of 18 research professorships, divided into mathematics, physics, chemistry, geology, economics, history, philosophy, literature, politics, and Chinese law, and are held by Gley, Zeng Zhaolun, Rao Yuqin, and Osgu, among others). C. Subsidized institutions: This year, there are a total of 19 subsidized institutions, of which 9 are schools, 6 are academic organizations, and 4 are educational and cultural organizations.

United Kingdom. The United Kingdom's return of the Boxer Indemnity, according to the exchange of notes between China and the United Kingdom in September 1919, stipulates that the total amount to be returned from December 1922 to February 1945 is £6,933,319.9 shillings in principal and £4,253,28.4 shillings in interest, totaling £11,186,547.13 shillings (the 4% interest deducted by the Chinese government customs must still be subtracted from this amount), specifically for mutual development purposes between the two countries. The method is to first use the funds as loans to develop railway construction and other productive industries, and then use the interest from the loans to develop educational and cultural endeavors. In the past four years, the funds have been used to develop productive industries, such as reorganizing and constructing railways, developing water conservancy, developing basic industries, developing gas business, and reorganizing transportation. There are a total of 25 cases, and the interest is used to support cultural endeavors, such as subsidizing the construction costs of the National Central Museum and the National Library by 1.5 million yuan each, allocated in installments over the years, establishing six professorships, each with an annual subsidy of 10,000 yuan for a period of three years, distributed among Central University, Zhongshan University, Wuhan University, Zhejiang University, the Beiyang Technical College, and the Central Institute of Physical and Chemical Research, and subsidizing the Central Research Institute's manufacturing of scientific instruments and equipment at a cost of 100,000 yuan, allocated in three installments, a subsidy of 100,000 yuan to the Peking Research Institute, with 69,000 yuan to subsidize the Physics Research Institute and 90,000 yuan to subsidize the Chemistry Research Institute, allocated in three installments, and subsidizing the equipment costs of the Nankai Mathematics Department and the equipment costs of Peking University and the Xiangya Medical College of the Scottish Church Medical College, the construction costs of the Shanghai Medical College, the National Institute of Compilation and Translation, and the Sino-British Cultural Association, and the compilation of books and atlases by the China Society for the Study of Architecture, and overseas study expenses of 180,000 yuan. Over the years, students have been sent to the UK for further study, and there have been awards for topics such as history textbooks for senior primary schools, songs for elementary schools, and public education lectures, as well as subsidies for special education expenses, and subsidies for the construction of elementary schools in Ningxia and Qinghai. In total, various types of allocations amount to 1.336 million yuan (the above is the amount of subsidies allocated in the 23rd year, while in the 24th year, there were subsidies for equipment expenses for Yunnan University and Guangxi University, and award funds for history textbooks for junior middle schools in Guizhou, as well as subsidies for the construction of the Xijing Midwifery School in Shaanxi and the construction of Mongolian and Tibetan elementary schools in Qinghai, and continued subsidies for various types of expenses from the 23rd year, totaling 1.3365 million yuan. In addition, 130,000 yuan was withdrawn from the reserve fund, with 100,000 yuan subsidized to the Ministry of Education for promoting short-term compulsory education in the provincial capitals of Qinghai, Ningxia, and Gansu provinces, and 30,000 yuan was used in conjunction with the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture to order 100 sets of physics experiment equipment for secondary schools from the Physics Research Institute of the Academia Sinica, of which 71 sets were sold at half price to senior middle schools in provinces such as Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, Sichuan, Guangdong, Shandong, Shanxi, Hebei, and Henan, and cities such as Beijing, Shanghai, Qingdao, etc., and the remaining 29 sets were all donated to senior middle schools run by overseas Chinese in provinces such as Yunnan, Guizhou, Sichuan, Suiyuan, Chahar, Shaanxi, Gansu, Xinjiang, and Qinghai). Its expenditure principles are based on using the funds for educational and cultural buildings with permanent commemorative significance and important cultural undertakings related to the whole country, and shall not be used to subsidize the regular expenses or temporary expenses of any institutions. It should also give appropriate consideration to the central government and cultural centers throughout the country, so as to make the undertakings have a broad and effective impact, and supplement the shortcomings of domestic education and culture. Educational and cultural undertakings are divided into five categories: A. Construction of the Central Library, the Central Museum, and preservation of indigenous cultural relics; B. Higher education and research institutions (with special emphasis on agriculture, engineering, medicine, and physics); C. Scholarships for studying abroad and overseas education undertakings; D. Awards for specialized works and textbooks for vocational schools in middle and lower classes; E. Establishing model elementary and middle schools, agricultural and vocational schools, midwifery schools, and developing rural education. The proportion of allocation for each category is: 25% for Category A, 35% for Category B, 15% for Category C, 1% for Category D, and 24% for Category E. As for the annual income of the British Boxer Indemnity in the future, the annual income from 1935 to 1940 is £596,481.5 shillings and 9 pence, the annual income from 1941 to 1945 is £412,127.15 shillings and 4 pence, and the income in 1946 is £596,481.5 shillings and 9 pence (the 4% interest deducted by the Chinese customs must be deducted from all of the above). The repayment period ends in 1946. The institution managing the Boxer Indemnity is the Board of Trustees for Rehabilitation Affairs of the British Boxer Indemnity Fund, which is subordinate to the Executive Yuan of China and was established in April 1923. The Chinese trustees are Zhu Jiahua and ten others, and the British trustees are Archibald Rose and five others. The association is located in Nanjing.

Ministry of Education Orders the Issuance of Measures for Dividing Elementary School Districts in Cities and Counties

(Nanjing News) The Ministry of Education revised the measures for dividing elementary school districts in cities and counties and issued an order to all education departments and bureaus on the 4th to comply with and follow the following three points. The units for dividing elementary school districts in various localities must be divided uniformly within this year. Each military district must set up at least one short-term elementary school. The funding for this should be raised by each district itself in principle. Districts in need may be subsidized by the central government and provincial funds. Each joint district and district should establish a school board in accordance with the regulations to be responsible for handling compulsory education affairs in the district, and the competent educational administrative organs should formulate measures for rewarding and punishing students and implement them earnestly at the end of each year. The annual meeting of the China Education and Cinema Association closes.

The Annual Meeting of the China Education and Cinema Association Closes. New Directors and Supervisors are Elected. 26 Resolutions are Passed.

(Wuxi Correspondent) The China Educational Film Association held its fifth annual meeting at the Provincial Educational Institute in Sheqiao Town on the 3rd of this month. More than 100 members attended, as previously reported. It is now known that a total of 26 proposals were discussed at the meeting, which were summarized into seven categories by the General Affairs Section. A. Research and Production, consisting of cases 1 and 4, related to the research of film measurement tables, and case 4, on cooperation between domestic films and modern Chinese novelists to select stories from their works to create scripts, to be submitted to the next board of directors meeting for presentation to the Central Committee for approval. B. Production, consisting of cases 3, 8, 13, 14, and 25, related to the Children's Day commemorative film, the method for filming children's education, case 8, on requesting the association to write to the Central Photography Studio to produce 16-millimeter films for circulation by local social education institutions, case 13, on the association producing educational films during extraordinary times to universally implement vocational education and emphasize the inculcation of military awareness and production knowledge, case 14, on the association producing films that meet the curriculum standards of all levels of students in primary and secondary schools to assist education, and case 25, on requesting the Central Photography Studio to pay attention to the production of educational films. All of the above cases were handed over to the board of directors for handling. C. Reuters Claims It Did Not Attack the Chinese Soccer Team. Since There Was No Attack, There Is No Need for Correction. The Chinese Soccer Team's Trip to Europe Is Not Affected.

Regarding Reuters' overseas communication, which stated that the Chinese soccer team's players had professional qualities, Shen Shuliang issued a statement refuting it, which was taken very seriously by all parties. In order to clarify the truth, this reporter specifically visited the person in charge of the agency, who explained as follows: This article was a special communication from a newspaper in London, and the author's intention was entirely to promote the Chinese soccer team and had no intention of attacking the Chinese soccer team. Since there was no attack, there is no need for correction. As far as the two soccer associations in Shanghai are concerned, the hosts are all promoting soccer and losing money to subsidize it. Their purpose is not to make money, so there is no professionalism to speak of, unlike the British professional soccer associations that rely on ticket sales for their livelihood. As for the Chinese soccer team's trip to Europe to participate in the Olympics, Europeans will definitely not misunderstand the Chinese soccer association because of this article, so it can be guaranteed that there will be no impact. Finally, the person in charge said that this misunderstanding was entirely accidental and deeply regrettable.

In the second match between China's Zheng Zhaojia and France's Pu Zhaise, Pu's skills were obviously better. The game lasted only forty minutes. Pu Hongsi won the first set with 6-0. In the second set, Zheng Zhaojia had some good shots, and the landing point was very good, but in the end, Pu Zhaise still won with 6-0. Although Zheng Zhaojia won two games in the second set, Pu Zhaise still won with 6-2.

Grains: Flour and Wheat Price Declines Intensify

Following the morning market opening, flour prices for both near and far months continued the downward trend from yesterday. Opening prices immediately followed suit. Extensive selling by inland merchants and Shanghai factories of far-month contracts in recent days further fueled the bearish sentiment among both internal and external short sellers. While large external investors remained steady, many smaller players lost confidence and sought to exit positions. As a result, the flour market saw prices decline steadily. Selling pressure remained strong throughout the afternoon, causing the market to fall further. Trading only stabilized near the close when factory shorts stopped selling. However, with clear weather anticipated and prospects for a bountiful new wheat harvest, the flour market may experience another decline. Ultimately, near and far-month contracts each fell by approximately 3 fen.

After the morning market opening, the wheat market was pressured by continuous price declines. Large external investors paused their buying, while many floating long positions lost their conviction. Inland merchants and factories took advantage of the situation and sold off their holdings. Amid the liquidation of long positions and aggressive short selling, market prices naturally declined. However, near-month contracts were supported by limited spot availability, while far-month contracts were pressured by increased short selling. Closing prices for June and July each fell by 2 fen, August by 4 fen, and September by 5 fen. Factories also sought to lower spot purchase prices, but sellers remained firm due to limited arrivals and inventories. Yesterday, 300 bags of Shandong wheat were sold at 5.20 yuan per bag, according to reports.

Chun Qiu (Spring and Autumn - a literary and cultural section)

Snippets

— (Zhang Feng)

In the past, during the era of autocracy, young people's marriages were entirely dictated by their parents through matchmakers. It was a system subordinate to the authoritarian rule of the family head, aligning with the political system of the time. While this inevitably created many unhappy couples, it also allowed young people more opportunities to devote themselves to their studies, hoping for greater achievements in their future careers, as they could focus without distractions. Now, with freedom of love prevailing, marriage follows the increasing age and physiological changes of young people, immediately becoming their most pressing issue upon entering the world, one that they must resolve themselves. To seek a spouse, one must first study the knowledge and techniques of love; to ensure a reliable marriage, one must sacrifice a considerable amount of time for investigation. In this way, unhappy couples may not be entirely eliminated, but observing the increasing number of divorce cases, the prime of youth easily slips away like flowing water, leading to regret! Furthermore, it is evident that among so-called "transactional marriages," aside from a few men and women who claim to be modern but harbor ulterior motives, the majority of couples manage to live peacefully. This is not a matter of mere chance. Those enthusiastic proponents of freedom of love and autonomy in marriage should reconsider this!

Begonia

— Master of Paper Tent and Copper Vase Studio

Among spring flowers, the begonia is the most charming. When in bud, it resembles dots of rouge, as if about to be applied to the cheeks of a beautiful woman. Planting them near walls or stones is most picturesque. The trees are about eight feet tall, and the flowers have single or double petals, in both light red and deep red varieties. The Chang Le Zhi (Record of Lasting Happiness) states: "Begonia is red, but when grafted with quince, it turns white." The Suo Sui Lu (Record of Trifles) also states: "The nature of yellow begonia is similar to that of the begonia, with slightly round and deep green leaves, smooth and dissimilar. The flowers are initially goose-yellow when half-open, gradually becoming light yellow when fully bloomed." Hong Shi has a poem about yellow begonia, saying: "Like a beauty with a half-covered forehead in the Han palace, elegant and refined, worthy of being called a flower fairy, nature bestows a gentle grace, making up a beautiful appearance in a casual manner." Thus, it can be known that there are variations in color, from white to yellow.

Chen Si of Qiantang wrote a Begonia Handbook, with narratives and poems, totaling over ten thousand words, comparable to Wang Guan's Peony Handbook and Ouyang Xiu's Record of Peonies in Luoyang, all famous works about fragrant flowers.

According to ancient methods, to make begonia flowers fresh and abundant, one should water the roots with fermented grains on the winter solstice morning. Also, after the begonia flowers wither and bear fruit, prune them, so that the flowers will be abundant and without leaves in the following year.

Begonias have soft branches, long stems, and light red colors, with drooping flowers facing downward, known as weeping begonias. Those suitable for potted plants are called crabapple begonias. Those that are about ten to twenty feet tall, with dense branches and smooth stems, are called Xifu begonias.

Begonias have scandalous histories. The Wai Shi Tao Wu (Unofficial History of Tao Wu) states: "Pan Kang of Shu had a favored concubine named Jie Chou, whose surname was Zhao. Her mother conceived her by swallowing begonia flower stamens. She possessed extraordinary beauty and was skilled in creating new melodies." The Leng Zhai Ye Hua (Night Talks from the Cold Studio) states: "The Emperor Emeritus ascended the Agarwood Pavilion and summoned Consort Yang. At that time, she was still drowsy from her midday nap. He ordered strong men to assist the maids in supporting her to come. The consort, with her tipsy charm and disheveled makeup, with her hair and ornaments in disarray, was unable to perform the proper bows. The Emperor Emeritus smiled and said, 'Is it that the consort is drunk? It is that the begonia has not slept enough.'"

In the Jiangnan region, begonias are called "Chuan Hong" (Sichuan Red). Wu Zhongfu's poem says: "Regretting that the beautiful spring season favors the land of Shu, there is no color like Sichuan Red." Its name is quite peculiar.

The Spring and Autumn Editorial Department of Shen Bao

Experiment

— Manzi

One day, I met Mr. Hong Shen. He told me that he had recently written a script for the Star Film Company called "New and Old Shanghai," which was an experiment. In this script, there are no main characters; all the performers are expected to develop equally, making the most of their strengths. The story has no cause and effect; society is the cause, and the representation of facts is the effect. The result is very scattered and complex. This kind of writing is creative for the individual, but it is rare in both the horizontal and vertical aspects.

I learned that Mr. Cheng Bugao was directing the script, so I went to visit him. He said that this film was also an experiment for him. In Star's past style, it has been almost consistent, always using many actors to perform a very grand story, adopting many scenes, and shooting a very complex structure. But directing a broad social reflection in a very simple setting is unprecedented. It's like a one-act play, but it has to contain the quality of a multi-act play, which is so difficult.

After listening to them, I was eager to see their work. At the preview the day before yesterday, I took two full hours to appreciate it, and I felt that both of their experiments had achieved considerable success. Generally, a comedy aims to amuse people, but after watching "New and Old Shanghai," after laughing for a while, there is a bit of a stimulating bittersweet taste. From a literary and artistic standpoint, the merit of the script lies in the sharpness of the dialogue. The merit of the performance lies in the humor of the actions. So I said to Mr. Zhou Jianyun, this is your boldness!

Swapped Phoenixes

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter One: Enjoying Tea and Having a Quiet Conversation While Listening to the Rain at the Night Window; Being Amazed by a Blossoming Branch Reflecting Fragrance in the Flower Alley

On that handsome face, adding a pair of crystal spectacles, two bright and radiant eyeballs, hiding an air of sharp wit under the glasses, he smiled. Guo Qi said, "You've been looking at me for a long time, suddenly smiling slightly, there seems to be something behind that." Ping Shan repeatedly tapped the floor with one foot, but his eyes were still scrutinizing Guo Qi. Guo Qi smiled and asked, "Why don't you speak? Don't you believe what I said?" Ping Shan replied, "Look, you are such a cultivated and dashing person, yet the texts you publish are always novels and notes with an air of sorrow and beauty, which are all manifestations of great tenderness. With the manifestation of tenderness, can you say there is no thought of a family in his heart?" Guo Qi smiled and said, "You've misunderstood my meaning." After saying that, he couldn't think of what to say next, so he could only raise both hands to adjust his spectacles. Then he stood up again, put the Venus statue on the table back in its place, and poured himself a cup of tea to drink. But just as he was about to pick up the cup, he put it down again and smiled slightly. Ping Shan said with a smile, "Brother Guo Qi, I see you like this, as if you have something to say. Why don't you speak it out?" Guo Qi smiled and said, "Of course, there is something to say, but if I were to say it, it would be a very long story, inevitably verbose. I think that marriage is a major event in life, and if the other party is even slightly reluctant, it would be better to have none at all. So, in my heart, that person must be like this Venus statue, pure and dustless, so that just seeing the surface, I feel a kind of admiration. This admiration must not be desire, must not be foolishness, must not be..." As he said this, he picked up the teacup on the table and put it to his lips, slowly sipping, with a slight smile, concentrating, trying to complete that sentence. Ping Shan smiled and said, "You don't need to say the rest. I already understand. It is to create a new and perfect family under pure love, nourishing your life in..." As he spoke, he raised his hand and kept scratching his ears and cheeks. Guo Qi smiled and said, "Love is a mysterious thing, which can never be described in words. Love that can be described in words is a very ordinary thing. In short, I know that my goals are set too high, and I can't find my ideal person in society. Precisely because I can't find my ideal person, I might as well be a bachelor." The conversation had already reached late at night. There were no sounds of people around, but there were raindrops blown by the wind, pattering against the branches of the trees and bamboo in the courtyard. Even though the windows in the room were all closed, a draft was constantly seeping in from the cracks in the window frames, and they both felt a kind of indescribable atmosphere. (17)

Special Feature One

Half-Hour Interview with Anna May Wong

— Wu Si (Selfless)

On the eve of Anna May Wong's visit to Hangzhou, I unexpectedly encountered her, who had just spent the day with Hu Die, at the towering, skyscraper-like Cathay Hotel. I should now refer to her as "Anna May Wong" or "Miss Amy". I had a long conversation with her in half an hour.

Knowing that Miss Wong was not accustomed to hearing Shanghainese, I pulled over a friend who could speak Cantonese to introduce us to her. I then asked her questions, with the tone and demeanor of a judge or detective. I felt a bit embarrassed for myself. However, Miss Wong, who was used to social events, answered us very frankly. No matter how trivial or abrupt the questions were, she always answered with a soft and gentle voice. This interview gave us a very good impression. It also provided us with a lot of information about her past and her achievements in film. What is written below is based on her own narration.

Anna May Wong's Signature

I am from Taishan, Guangdong, and I am thirty years old this year. I was born in San Francisco, USA. My father's name is Liang Ren, and he has been doing business in Los Angeles, USA, running a laundry. I have seven siblings in total, and none of us are married. I am the second oldest. I have a younger brother who is teaching in Shanghai, and a younger sister who works in the customs. I started filming when I was fifteen years old. First, I signed a contract with Universal Film Company. In the past ten years, I have signed contracts with MGM, United Artists, and Paramount in the United States. In Europe, I have also signed contracts with Gaumont in England and UFA in Germany. I have filmed several films, including "The Toll of the Sea," "Piccadilly," "Shanghai Express," "Limehouse Blues," and "Java Head," but I am not very satisfied with them. This time, I came back to my homeland to see more of the actual situation in China. I hope to be able to interact with people from all walks of life in the domestic society, especially with the women in Chinese families. At the same time, I want to learn to speak Chinese more. Because when I was young, I only studied Chinese for four years, and for the rest of the past twenty years, I have been speaking American English. Chinese people in the United States can understand American English, but in China, it is not enough to speak Cantonese alone. It is necessary to be able to speak standard Mandarin. Soon, most likely next week, I will go to Beiping to spend the summer vacation, or there will be more opportunities to learn Chinese Mandarin. Most likely in September of this year, I will still have to return to Shanghai and then go to the United States. The roles I have played in films before were not very important. I obeyed the director's commands and often played Chinese women in foreign scripts. The roles I played were mostly maids or concubines. In the future, I do not want to take on such roles again. I hope that someone will use British people to write several film scripts depicting modern Chinese society or family life to provide to American companies for filming. At the same time, I also plan to contribute what I have observed during my travels to the American film industry for reference.

Anna May Wong, who speaks fluent foreign language, if she didn't have yellow skin, black hair, flat nose, and almond-shaped eyes, I really wouldn't believe that she was a Chinese woman.

Special Feature Two

A Visit to the First Laborers' Nursery

— Ya Fei

For a working family or a working woman, having a child can indeed become a problem. Because once a woman has a child, she inevitably has to shoulder a considerable responsibility for nurturing and educating them. This is, of course, the duty of a general housewife, and those with sufficient wealth can hire nannies or wet nurses to take care of it. However, for working or laboring women, they cannot abandon their original jobs or careers for the sake of family finances. Hiring a wet nurse is even more unlikely. Furthermore, factories, commercial firms, and institutions in our country do not yet have "nursery rooms" or "lactation rooms" specially set up for female employees and workers like those in Europe and America. Thus, in this situation, they face the difficulty of attending to one thing and neglecting the other.

Currently, there are many debates about whether women should enter society or return to the family. However, I believe there is no problem with either going to the family or going to society. Anyway, there are things they should do both at home and in society. However, the first thing to consider is to ensure that both sides benefit without harm.

Yesterday, I made a special trip to the vicinity of Banfang on Penglai Road in the Nanshi area to visit the First Laborers' Nursery founded by the city's Children's Welfare Association. I felt that it was an institution that specifically accepts entrusted childcare from laboring families and working women. Unfortunately, the scale is too small, and the number of children inside is limited, which inevitably makes people feel regretful. However, according to the authorities' original intention, they may want to expand to the first, second, third, and even ninth and tenth locations. However, to this day, a second Laborers' Nursery has yet to appear.

I stepped into the door, explained my intentions to a servant, and waited in the reception room. There, in addition to the photos of the members of the Children's Welfare Association, such as Wu Tiecheng, Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, and Li Ting'an, there were also various slogans and regulations on the wall. Soon, Ms. Zhang, the administrator, came to lead me to visit various departments and told me about all the facilities in the center.

There are a total of six buildings here. The downstairs is the office, examination room, reception room, etc. Upstairs, on the left is the infant department, which has a total of thirty infants, each with a small white iron bed. All clothes and bedding are made of white flannel. They are entirely breastfed, and the monthly fee is twelve yuan. All needs and clothing are borne by the center. This department accepts babies from four months to more than ten months old. Each baby is set for a period of fifteen months, and after the period expires, the parents take them back, and new babies are accepted.

On the right is the children's department. In addition to the children's bedroom, exercise room, dining room, and bathroom, there is also a classroom. There are also thirty or so children there, aged two to four. The monthly fee is only two yuan, and clothes and food are provided by the center. However, they do not stay overnight at the center. The children's parents send them in at seven o'clock every morning and pick them up at six o'clock in the afternoon. As for life, they have two hours of classes every morning, three meals a day, and must take a nap for two hours from one to three o'clock in the afternoon. They change clothes every other day and take a bath at least once a week.

The bedroom is specially for their nap. There are more than thirty small iron beds arranged in a row, each with bedding. The light in the room is kept soft. The exercise room is filled with various toys and sports equipment. The thirty or so lively, innocent, and lovely children are playing in the room.

All the departments are clean and tidy, filled with an atmosphere of love and happiness. You can't hear any noise or crying inside.

The center employs twelve young and strong nannies and wet nurses to nurture and manage the children. Regarding health, a special doctor comes to the center every week to check the children's bodies and mouths, and those with diseases are sent to the hospital for treatment.

After returning from the visit, I felt that this is indeed a social undertaking worth promoting, and I hope everyone will cherish it.

Shen Bao Literary Supplement

Research on the Science of Moxibustion (Part 1)

— Xie Yunshou

Moxibustion is one of the ancient medical methods in our country. It is prevalent among the people, and ignorant old women can perform it. To say it is ineffective is belied by its continued transmission to this day, and the occasional appearance of remarkable effects. To say it is effective may not be entirely true. In this way, the method has been practiced for thousands of years, with everyone knowing that it is so, but not knowing why it is so. Now, from a scientific point of view, I will explain the truth of moxibustion as follows.

(A) The History of Moxibustion: Treating diseases by causing burns to the skin. The origin of this method probably began in ancient China. However, some people say that it originated in India, but there is no definite proof. Moxibustion is also prevalent in Japan. It was transmitted from our country in 1222 AD. During the Azuchi-Momoyama period in Japan, there were also writings on moxibustion. There should be many such writings in our country, but most of them are handwritten copies. Even those that are printed are difficult to reproduce faithfully due to the crude drawings. Moreover, almost all handwritten copies are secret books that people are unwilling to circulate. This is also a major reason for the backwardness of Chinese medicine.

(B) The Definition of Moxibustion: The so-called moxibustion is the method of treating diseases by placing moxa leaves on a specific point on the skin (the so-called acupuncture point) and burning it with fire.

(C) The Burning Temperature During Moxibustion: When moxa is burned, it can generate a temperature of 640 degrees Celsius. However, when using moxa cones and burning them on the abdominal wall of a rabbit, the average temperature is between 61 and 200 degrees Celsius. The temperature reaching under the skin, such as reaching a depth of two centimeters, can rise by about two degrees. If it reaches a depth of two and three-tenths of a centimeter, the increase is less than half a degree.

The above burning of moxa cones acts on the tissues of the skin, causing the proteins to coagulate to a certain extent. The coagulated proteins are gradually broken down and absorbed, resulting in a type of foreign protein reaction.

(D) The Effect of Moxibustion on Various Parts of the Body: Effects on Blood: Within two minutes after applying moxibustion to a rabbit, its blood is taken for examination, and an increase in white blood cells is observed, reaching 34% or even double. The cells that increase at this time are mostly neutrophils. This increase in white blood cells can continue for four or five days after the moxibustion is applied. Some people also say that red blood cells and hemoglobin also increase. In addition, the blood clotting time is shortened, and there is an increase in blood sugar. The sedimentation rate of blood cells is also increased.

Also, after applying moxibustion to a rabbit, taking its blood and separating its serum can prove an increase in adrenaline-like substances.

Effects on Blood Vessels: Blood vessels first constrict and then dilate after moxibustion.

Effects on Pulse: The pulse rate increases when the moxa is burning. The pulse rate remains high after the fire is extinguished until the blood vessels dilate.

Effects on Blood Pressure: In animal experiments, blood pressure initially rises due to the momentary stimulation of pain when moxibustion is applied. After the stimulation is removed, it drops and returns to normal within a short time. The degree of change varies depending on the type of animal and the size of the moxibustion. In humans, there are also cases of increased blood pressure, typically by 5-32 mmHg.

Effects on Respiration: The respiratory rate often increases, sometimes decreases, and sometimes there is no effect.

Effects on Intestinal Movement: Usually, after applying moxibustion, the vigorous intestinal movement is calmed down. This is probably due to the stimulation of the sympathetic nerves controlling the intestines and the effect of adrenaline-like substances.

Effects on Bile Secretion: When a biliary fistula is created in a rabbit and moxibustion is applied, an increase in bile secretion is observed. However, when "Atropin" is used to inhibit the sympathetic nerves, the bile secretion does not increase. This increase is probably due to the hyperactivity of the sympathetic nervous system.

Effects on Muscle Strength and Fatigue: Applying moxibustion during muscle work results in increased muscle strength and rapid recovery from fatigue. This is probably due to the increased production of adrenaline.

Effects on the Kidneys: Experiments on rabbits show that moxibustion does not have a diuretic effect. If the degree of moxibustion is increased, leaving a large scar, proteinuria is observed.

A Global Perspective on Tuberculosis Statistics (VII)

— Ding Huikang

Regarding the so-called two types of statistics, namely, the tuberculosis mortality rate for those under 30 years old, the rate for the entire territory of Germany is lower than the statistics for Prussia. From 30 to 70 years old, the two are almost equal. After 70 years old, the statistics for Prussia are lower. In the death cases under the age of five, there has been a decreasing phenomenon in both the Prussian province and the entire territory of Germany before 1930. However, there has been a tendency to increase between 1931 and 1932. The mortality rate for men during their youth working years has also gradually decreased. The mortality rate for women between the ages of five and thirty is higher than that for men.

The following table shows the statistics of tuberculosis mortality in various age groups of both sexes by Moellers.

First year: More men than women

Second year to tenth year: Men equal women

Tenth to twentieth years adolescence: More women than men

Twentieth to twenty-fifth years: More men than women (1882 to 1922)

More women than men (1923 to 1929)

Twenty-fifth to thirtieth years: More men than women (1882 to 1902)

More women than men (starting in 1913)

The following table shows the tuberculosis mortality statistics for both sexes in various age groups in Germany (units of 10,000 residents).

According to Calmette's report, the tuberculosis mortality rate for infants in a tuberculous environment is 24-80%. Lederer and Retse in Germany found only 5.1-7.1%. Goetzel in Austria and Frautz also had similar numbers, at 7%. However, Frautz proved that the tuberculosis mortality rate for infants was higher, at 16.9%. From this point of view, the average tuberculosis mortality rate for infants in tuberculous environments is not as high as previously estimated.

In fact, the tuberculosis mortality rate for infants in a tuberculous environment does not decrease after BCG vaccination. However, there is still a lack of large-scale statistics on this point. Looking at the infant mortality statistics in a tuberculous infectious environment in Berlin, it is not higher than elsewhere. In Düsseldorf, infants with tuberculosis infection are comparatively safer, and the statistics may even be slightly lower. In fact, on the one hand, it is due to the organization of a large number of clinics and protection centers, and on the other hand, the decline in this mortality statistic is also related to the simultaneous decrease in tuberculosis mortality and the number of births during the women's childbearing period.

Young children's tuberculosis mortality rates also have the same good trend. In Bonn, Frentzen performed the Moro reaction test on 393 children under the age of six in the clinic. 110 cases were negative, and 162 cases were positive, but no clinical or X-ray pathological changes were found.

The mortality rate for school-age children has also gradually decreased. Peretti, Kieffer, and Stephan have all provided the same evidence. What needs to be noted is that new infections in girls are more common than in boys during school age. This first tuberculosis infection is most tolerable during school age than at any other age. According to Braeuning's statistics, only 5% of school-age children have a tuberculosis infection each year, acute tuberculosis accounts for 1.8%, and open tuberculosis accounts for only 0.1%. Peretti and Simon conducted large-scale examinations in various places. Simon found that 30.3% in urban schools and 22.6% in rural schools in the Allenburg area had positive results. The reasons for this decrease in infection are partly due to the improvement of school facilities and partly due to the immediate isolation of patients after the disease is discovered. Peretti proved that 30.1% had a positive reaction to the Moro method in 1925, and only 12.5% in 1932. After leaving school life, the statistics were 54.3% in 1927 and 40.4% in 1933. From this point of view, the total transmission of tuberculosis is not in the initial period of childhood, but at a higher age. The spread of tuberculosis, whether in infancy, childhood, or school age, is mostly related to external causes, and the economic relationship of the parents is even more important.

Young children's tuberculosis mortality rate has been slightly increasing before 1931, but in recent years, the statistics have stopped and decreased again. Langer's clinical statistics from the Queen Victoria Hospital in Berlin from 1926 to 1931 also proved an increase in young children with tuberculosis.

What is the degree of danger to school-age children with teachers with open tuberculosis? The results of G:ertbmuhlen's experiment showed that 32% of a female teacher with open tuberculosis had a positive tuberculin reaction, while only 21% of healthy teachers had a positive reaction. In other experimental methods, there were also huge differences, with a ratio of 79.5% to 38.7%.

The mortality rate of infants at risk of tuberculosis infection in the United Kingdom has also decreased comparatively. This is Cox's report. His observation is the same as that in Germany, which is closely related to the problems of clinics, nursing homes, and nutrition. He also proved that the mortality rate between the first and second years is the same, and the mortality rate of young children aged between the second and fifth years in a tuberculous environment has increased significantly. The positive tuberculin reaction is more common in young children in a tuberculous infectious environment than in a non-tuberculous infectious environment (Schlesinger), and the largest number of infections is five years in a dangerous infectious environment and fifteen years in a non-tuberculous environment. Also, girls are often more infected than boys. The degree of infection of fathers with tuberculosis is also higher than that of mothers with tuberculosis.

Common Sense on Hygiene for Ear, Nose, Throat and Eye Diseases

— Tang Renjin

(Eighty-seven) Eyelid Abscess, Eyelid Boil, and Eyelid Spasm

Eyelid Abscess: Eyelid abscesses are mostly caused by damage to the skin of the eyelid or secondary to orbital periostitis and erysipelas. It starts with redness and swelling of the local skin. A hard knot gradually rises under the skin, causing pain. The preauricular lymph nodes are also often swollen, and sometimes fever occurs. After a while, the subcutaneous infiltration part can soften into pus. At this time, if an incision is made, the pus can be drained and cured.

Eyelid Boil: The cause of eyelid boils is the same as that of ordinary boils. It is also caused by the infection of staphylococcus. It usually occurs in the eyebrow area. It initially presents as a papule or pustule. The surrounding skin is red and swollen. Soon, the induration gradually increases, and the local area feels painful. In severe cases, there are chills and fever. The treatment for this disease is to first use anti-inflammatory methods. If pus points appear, an incision should be made to drain the pus.

Eyelid Spasm: Eyelid spasm is caused by the spasmodic contraction of the orbicularis oculi muscle, causing the patient to involuntarily close the eyelids. The causes can be divided into two types.

Symptomatic Eyelid Spasm - When there are foreign bodies in the conjunctival sac (such as dust blowing into the eyes), ingrown eyelashes, corneal herpes, corneal ulcers, iritis, etc., the trigeminal nerve can often be stimulated, causing a kind of reflex action, which causes the orbicularis oculi muscle to spasm. At this time, the patient's eyelids are closed and not easily opened. Tears flow frequently, making it difficult for doctors to examine the eyelids. An eyelid retractor must be used, or eye drops that reduce irritation must be instilled to achieve the purpose of examination. The treatment principle is to treat the primary disease in order to hope for recovery.

Idiopathic Eyelid Spasm - This disease is the primary spasm of the orbicularis oculi muscle. It is mostly caused by hysteria, so this disease is also called hysteric eyelid spasm. The spasm is particularly strong when the spirit is excited. Furthermore, an eyelid spasm that occurs in the elderly is called senile eyelid spasm. It is also a type of idiopathic spasm.

Domestic Medicinal Plants (Continued)

— Zhou Mengbai

(V) Loofah Luffa cylindrica, Roem. Luffa (English)

(Plant) Native to the tropics, it can be cultivated everywhere. It is an annual vine herb. Leaves alternate, petiolate, palmate, with sharp or shallow lobes, uneven serrated green, acute tips. Monoecious. In summer and autumn, it blooms yellow unisexual flowers, male flowers are racemose, female flowers are solitary. The berry is long cylindrical, rich in reticulated fibers.

(Ingredients) The water that flows out when its stem is cut is the so-called "loofah water", which contains niter. Other ingredients are still unknown.

(Medicinal) Folk: Loofah water can be used as a cough suppressant and diuretic.

(Other uses) Loofah water can be used as a lotion.

When growing vigorously in summer, collect the above-ground stems, cut each section into 30 cm. Insert the stem opening of the upper part into a bottle to obtain loofah water. After one day and night, about 500 cc of loofah water can be obtained.

Loofah fiber, commonly known as "loofah sponge", can be used for various scrubbing purposes.

Valerianaceae

1. Patrinia Patrinia scabiosaefolia, Link.

(Plant) Self-grown in the mountains and fields, it is a perennial herb. The stem is about ——1.5 meters high. The root leaves are pinnately mid-lobed, the lobes are obovate with blunt tips. The stem leaves are opposite, pinnately deeply lobed, the lobes are narrow and long, with notched edges, and the green is like serrated teeth. Axillary corymbose inflorescences, in autumn, small yellow flowers bloom. The achene is small and long oval.

(Medicinal) Old sayings: Patrinia root is used to treat carbuncles, edema, and postpartum abdominal pain. Used as a decoction.

Prescription example: Coix Seed, Aconite, and Patrinia Powder two

Coix seed 4.0 Aconite 1.0 Patrinia 2.0

The above is made into a decoction of 100, to be taken as a single dose.

2. Valerian Valeriana officinalis, L. Tar. Angustifolia, Mig.

(Plant) Self-grown in the mountains and can be cultivated. It is a perennial herb. The stems and leaves are slender. The leaves are opposite, with three to five pairs of pinnately completely lobed lobes. The lobes are linear lanceolate with blunt serrated edges. Terminal umbellate inflorescences, small light red flowers bloom in early summer. The fruits are small and have pappus.

Western valerian V. Officinalis, L. is not much different from valerian, except that the lobes of the leaves are quite narrow.

Mountain valerian V. Fincidissima, Maxim. is similar in shape to valerian, slightly smaller, and has soft creeping branches. The roots have a very slight valerian odor. Not for medicinal use.

(Cultivation method) Start dividing the plants in early October, with a bed width of two feet, and a spacing of about one foot between each plant. In May and June of the following year, carry out two cultivations. Fertilizers include compost, basal fertilizer, and rice bran. In early May, the flower spikes are extracted, and at this time, cut off the stem three inches from the ground to promote the growth of the roots. Harvest in late August, with a yield of about 100 catties of fresh roots per mu.

(Crude drug) Valerian Root Rhizoma Valeriance is made by collecting and drying the rhizomes and roots. The rhizome is 2 cm long and 1 cm thick, with buds and residual stems at the upper end. The surrounding roots are about 2 mm thick and about 20 cm long, and the roots are mostly branched. The surface is yellowish-brown or dark brown, and the texture is brittle. This product has a unique pungent aroma and a slightly spicy taste.

Common Sense Q&A on Teeth (31)

— Lin Jianxian

(Question 149) Why shouldn't we eat foods that are too cold or too hot?

Answer: Foods that are too cold or too hot have excessive stimulating power, and the dental pulp is easily affected. It is not advisable to eat them often.

(Question 150) Why are acidic foods harmful to teeth?

Answer: Overly acidic foods such as sour fruits and vinegar can directly erode the dental enamel. It is not advisable to eat them often. If you eat them occasionally, you must rinse your mouth afterward.

(Question 151) Are sugary foods as harmful as ordinary people imagine?

Answer: Sugar is a type of carbohydrate, just like rice and wheat. It does not directly damage teeth. If you say that sugar is harmful to teeth and should not be eaten, then rice and wheat should not be eaten either! However, the residue left in the mouth when eating sugar, like the residue from rice and noodles, is very easy to ferment and turn sour. Acidity can dissolve the dental enamel. If you eat it at the right time, eat it with other things during meals, and brush your teeth afterward, then sugary foods will not be harmful. However, it is better for those who do not brush their teeth after eating to eat less.

(Question 152) What should be paid attention to in the diet during pregnancy?

Answer: During pregnancy, teeth are more prone to decay due to the loss of lime in the body. At this time, you should eat more nutritious foods. Products rich in lime and vitamin D are quite suitable.

Section 5: Overall Health and Other Considerations

(Question 153) How does overall poor health affect teeth?

Answer: People with declining health mostly have poor nutrition, and their metabolism is out of balance. There is too much oxygen in the body, the dental enamel deteriorates, and the resistance is weak. Saliva also often becomes abnormal, even becoming acidic, losing the function of protecting teeth. Tooth decay and other dental problems are prone to occur. Tooth problems can further weaken the body. Therefore, statistically speaking, most of the people who seek treatment for dental problems from dentists are unhealthy.

(Question 154) Why do many people in the countryside have healthy teeth even though their diet is poor and they do not pay attention to oral hygiene?

Answer: People in rural areas work at sunrise and rest at sunset. Their lives are very natural and simple, and there are very few things that harm their health. They can also get sunlight and fresh air, so their bodies are relatively healthy and have fewer diseases. Therefore, their teeth also have relatively strong resistance and are not easily decayed. Many teeth of savage tribes and ancient people were very intact, which was also due to their good health.

A Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (89)

— Hu Jiayan

How should the sputum of patients with this disease be disposed of? Its sole purpose, of course, is to eradicate the tuberculosis bacteria in the sputum! As mentioned above, tuberculosis bacteria are highly resistant and extremely difficult to kill. Therefore, before detailing various eradication methods, it is necessary to understand the true state of their resistance. Their (tuberculosis bacteria's) resistance to dryness, putrefaction, and cold is astonishing. In ordinary dry places, the lifespan of tuberculosis bacteria in sputum can extend to more than nine months; naturally, there are slight differences depending on sunlight exposure and the thickness of the sputum layer. Generally, thicker sputum clumps last longer than thinner layers, and those without sunlight exposure last longer than those with sunlight exposure; the longest survival occurs in dark corners of rooms where thick clumps form. Secondly, resistance to putrefaction is much weaker than the former, but it still takes at least several days to die. Thirdly, bacteria are generally indifferent to cold; in fact, it is the best condition for preserving their lives, completely different from humans who cannot tolerate cold and freeze to death. Tuberculosis bacteria are no exception. Even after being subjected to ten degrees below freezing point for six weeks, their infectivity remains unchanged. In addition, one thing must be stated incidentally: many people bury the sputum-contaminated clothing of patients in the soil, believing that tuberculosis bacteria will die as a result; this is completely wrong. Because there is no sunlight or air in the soil, it is difficult for putrefaction to occur; on the contrary, it becomes the best condition for their survival. According to expert reports, viable tuberculosis bacteria can still be found in the lungs of patients who have been buried in the soil for more than two years, which gives us a glimpse of the situation!

How can tuberculosis bacteria be killed? The methods currently used in medicine are roughly limited to: disinfectants and bactericides; heating; and utilizing sunlight. Details of these aspects will now be described below:

Disinfectants and bactericides: Carbolic acid is the most common bactericide, but if it is mixed with sputum containing tuberculosis bacteria, it takes a long time; approximately 5% carbolic acid solution requires at least 24 hours to kill the tuberculosis bacteria. Pure alcohol is similar, but the amount of alcohol must be more than ten times the amount of sputum to be effective. Concentrated mercuric chloride solution takes less time, but its effect is difficult to reach the center of the sputum, so many people do not advocate its use. Alkalysol, a preparation of Kresal, has been widely used recently; approximately 5% solution requires about four hours at ordinary temperature; if heated to 80 degrees Celsius, it only takes half an hour; for washing, a 2% solution is sufficient. Gb. Bacillol is also a preparation of Kresal, and its function is roughly the same as the former, with a dosage of 5% solution. Chloramin is also popular because it has no odor; a 10% solution is needed, requiring six hours; if used to wipe the floor (in the patient's room), 1% is sufficient. For sputum attached to fingers or clothing, washing the area with a thousandth concentration of mercuric chloride or a 5% carbolic acid solution can kill most of the tuberculosis bacteria immediately. For fingers suspected of having bacteria attached, simply washing them thoroughly with water and soap, along with disinfectant solution, can achieve the purpose of disinfection; this is a very simple method that can be implemented by senders and those who are close to patients every time and everywhere.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

The Problem of Bank Loans

— Zhou Ge

Member Ma Yinchu of the Legislative Yuan’s opinion on the rural revival plan includes a request for bank loans, saying: “The general opinion in the city is that the Central Bank should consider lowering bank loan interest rates from the perspective of the city's economy. However, lowering bank loan interest rates will also cause the interest rates on deposits to be lowered at the same time. Currently, foreign banks in China have raised deposit interest rates to six or seven percent. If domestic banks lower deposit interest rates, there is a risk of capital flowing into foreign banks, which should be considered carefully.”

China's financial industry is built on speculative businesses like government bonds and real estate, rather than on the development of industry; that is to say, it does not take industry as its foundation. This can be seen from bank loans. “Lowering bank loan interest rates will also cause the interest rates on deposits to be lowered at the same time.” However, if the interest rate on bank deposits increases, then the interest rate on bank loans will naturally increase as well. Once the lending rate increases, almost all industrial and commercial operators will be unable to borrow from banks, and the banks themselves, due to the semi-colonial nature of China's industry and commerce in the context of this global economic downturn, are also a little uneasy about industry and commerce. Therefore, the two are alienated from each other, that is, Chinese financial capital and industry and commerce.

If Chinese financial capital and industry and commerce are so alienated, then can Chinese financial capital be closely integrated with the vast masses of poor farmers in the hopelessly bankrupt rural areas? Since the interest rate on bank deposits cannot be lowered, and the interest rate on bank loans is of course unwilling to be lowered, the vast masses of poor farmers are still unable to obtain loans. And even if they do borrow money, they may fall into an even deeper debt pit in the future and be unable to extricate themselves. The tragic scene at that time can be seen simply by closing one's eyes. What is meant by the so-called "reviving the countryside"?

The problem lies here: “Currently, foreign banks have raised deposit interest rates to six or seven percent. If domestic banks lower deposit interest rates, there is a risk of capital flowing into foreign banks.” International financial capital is constantly tripping up our Chinese financial capital. If you want to move your hand or foot, or even twitch your eyeball, it will cause him

If we want Chinese financial capital to provide a little timely rain in this bankrupt countryside, or even cooperate well with our industry and commerce, the most fundamental thing is to get rid of the one who is tripping us up first!

May

— Yan Ting

The hot blood of Wen Kete flowed through his parched veins. He seemed to hear a torrent of roaring people, flooding every gap in the city of Chicago; he seemed to see thousands upon thousands of people's rough, dark fists waving before his eyes. However, when the singing from the basement suddenly stopped, he couldn't help but look around in surprise. His fantasy vanished, and the crowd and the roar disappeared into a vortex of silence and darkness. At this time, he felt a little anxious, as if a flame was burning in his heart. Due to the illusion, his nostrils inhaled a strong smell of alcohol. It greedily and powerfully attracted him. He reached into the pocket of his torn coat, feeling two smooth, fifty-cent silver coins, which were the bread for him and his family for three days. However, before he had time to think about it, he lifted his resolute steps and pushed open the basement door.

The basement was now darkly filled with people, a group of rough, dark, dirty people! Some were half drunk, some were completely drunk, some were young, some were old, there were men and women. This was a group of unfortunate people, oppressed by life. They raised their rough, dark fists and roared loudly for their misfortune.

"Brothers! What gift has President Roosevelt's economic recovery law given everyone? The huge unemployment of thirty million people!" A young man pounded the table with his fist, roaring angrily.

"And I've been unemployed for two whole years!" An aging little old man sighed in a painful and weak voice.

"Drink! Brothers, drink hard!"

"Come! This is our last cup!"

Wen Kete ran to the counter, ordered a bottle of strong ale, and secretly ran to a shady corner to drink it. The stimulation of the strong alcohol did not give him much waiting. His head became heavy, and his two dry eyes overflowed with bloodshot flames.

Night, with black wings, slipped away. It was when the last drop was left in his glass that he became blurred, and he felt that the world was burning. But a thought, a terrible horror seized him, when he reached into his pocket and groped, he discovered that he had committed a great crime. He had drunk the bread of his wife and children. They were hungry, crying, waiting for his return, waiting for his smooth, lovely two fifty-cent silver coins; but he had drunk it all. He thought of it, and he trembled slightly. His ears were as if stuffed with something, and he could not hear any sound; his eyes were as if blurred by something, and he could not see anything, only his wife's fierce face, her rude scolding, and the children's crying and faint moans of hunger...

He stood up from his seat sadly, stunned, and the cup he was holding fell to the ground unnaturally, ringing sharply and shattering.

Sealing the Door

— Chen Ji

As the morning light peeked out from the dim clouds, furtively crawling into Sister-in-law A Gen’s narrow and turbid little room, Sister-in-law A Gen’s heart was almost leaping out of her chest, and she couldn’t help but cry out.

Page 20

"Ah! It's the fifteenth!..."

Her whole body felt like it had been thrown into a fire, suffering from feverish pain, and she thought of her husband.

He hadn't had anything to do for more than a year, just loafing around at home, either quarreling with her or beating his six-year-old child, Mao Mao. Everything in the house had been pawned off! They lived day by day in hunger, cold, anxiety, and worry.

They were in debt; they were “second landlords,” using the rent collected from “third tenants” to temporarily fill their stomachs. In this way, the rent had been vacant for a full eight months.

"Mr. Accountant: Thank you, please help me, I'm about to have business! I will pay it off..."

A Gen said with very humble and pleading words, and the accountant left in a burst of restrained anger. They did not dare to use the rent collected from the third tenants to fill their stomachs again, and they borrowed from wherever they could borrow, borrow, borrow... but the rent was still in arrears for eight months.

"Ah! This is heaven helping us, isn't it." When Sister-in-law A Gen heard A Gen say very happily: "There's a letter from Hankou, there's a job in the cigarette factory there!" Her head tilted up to the sky, and a strong religious feeling suddenly arose in her heart.

Managing to borrow travel expenses, A Gen set off with a heart full of hope. He had said to his wife: "Take good care of the children. If things go well there, I will come to pick you up to live there with me." Sister-in-law A Gen shed tears of joy as she sent off her husband.

But a month, two months... the money A Gen sent back was still not enough to fill her and her children's stomachs, and the rent was still eight months in arrears. A Gen had not yet told her in his letters: "The factory business is very slow, not to mention night work, even day work, sometimes only two days a week can be done..." But the accountant did not know this hardship, and he came with bodyguards, saying so angrily:

"Now that your man has business! If you don't pay three months by the fifteenth, we're going to seal the door! The court ruled it long ago, didn't it? I only treated you leniently because I saw that your man had no business!"

Sister-in-law A Gen was so anxious that she quickly wrote a letter to A Gen there, but she received A Gen's reply: saying to discuss it with the accountant, and as soon as the business improved, he would definitely pay three months...

Sister-in-law A Gen led her two sons, and personally ran to the accountant's office to plead, but the answer she got: was still those few stern words.

But today is the fifteenth! Sister-in-law A Gen was sobbing and weeping. A six-year-old and a three-year-old, the two children's slight snores were playing in harmony with their mother's crying: how desolate the morning air was!

The fifteenth filled the earth with sunshine. The children were dragging Sister-in-law A Gen, wanting breakfast, but she was lost and bewildered, just staring at them with her red and swollen eyes.

The tenants told Sister-in-law A Gen to move out some furniture, but she did nothing, just like she was crazy, her chest rising and falling rapidly, and she stared blankly at the people surrounding her.

Finally, the misfortune that brought her ruin arrived. The accountant rushed in, followed by a bailiff, the doorman carrying wooden boards, silver heads, and the accountant shouted sternly:

"How's the rent?"

"Help me, please..."

"Seal the door! Seal the door!"

The bailiff dragged Sister-in-law A Gen out. The doorman nailed the wooden boards crisscrossed on the door, and her room was also sealed at the same time. The tenants were given three days to move out. At this time, Sister-in-law A Gen seemed to wake up, sitting in the alley, crying and screaming, and the two children were also crying and shouting by her side:

"Mommy! Mommy!..."

A large group of people surrounded her, as if sympathizing with her, and as if watching a spectacle.

Dust

— Xu Ji

In the morning, at the entrance of that noisy little teahouse, I met that strange "Mr. Lu" again; this time, he was no longer aimlessly wandering the streets with a sorrowful expression, or mentioning his "eighty-year-old mother" in a voice that seemed about to cry—this time, he was serious, as if he was in a hurry, looking out at the entrance of the little teahouse as if he was expecting something. When he saw me, he just nodded in surprise and turned away, looking at the traffic and people coming and going on the street as if nothing had happened.

I sized up that middle-aged man I had always called "Mr. Lu": I felt that, as he himself had said before, "I will finally fall from the tower of life one day," and now, perhaps he had really fallen from the "tower of life." He was wearing even more tattered clothes than before, and he had an even more withered appearance than before: "In short, life is getting worse day by day..."

However, the tower of life is steep and dangerous, and no one can guarantee that they won't fall one day! Yes, that strange "Mr. Lu," I watched him fall from life day by day, and I also saw his "attempts" at life, but "people will finally end so quickly"...

I met "Mr. Lu" in the attic of a house. Because we lived in the same house, because we met every morning and evening, we started by nodding to each other indifferently, then greeting each other, smiling, and saying a few usual idle words; in this way, we strangely became "acquainted"...

Everyone felt that this thin, vague "Mr. Lu" was a bit strange. It was said that he taught in a small school, earning twelve dollars a month. He taught seven or eight hours of classes every night, and used these twelve dollars, which were paid once every three months (!), to maintain the lives of three people besides himself: an eighty-year-old mother and two dirty children...

I never heard him mention the children's mother, and no one ever asked him about "Mrs. Lu." Only one summer evening, ten coppers of shochu had intoxicated his nerves, and he angrily cursed his woman, saying that "she looks down on poor men, leaves two children behind, and runs to rich young masters to be a mistress, shameless, this world, this world..."

But when he woke up the next day, he seemed to have forgotten everything and no longer mentioned it. And people no longer had the leisure to ask about things he didn't want to talk about...

In this way, day after day, Mr. Lu lived in endless frustration, living in worry. Late at night, he would quietly prepare a little for tomorrow's night classes, reading the sentences in "Qiu Shui Xuan Ruler" over and over again, shaking his head and wagging his tail, and also checking the "classics" he didn't know in a dilapidated "Ci Yuan" that he only had; however, after the school owed him four months' salary, even that dilapidated "Ci Yuan" was sold to the old bookstore for three cents...

As a result, Mr. Lu and his "family" were also driven away for owing several months' rent. When he left, he seemed to realize something, and said in a distorted way: "Life is originally a long and steep road. As you walk, people become covered in dust—as long as there is something that can make life better, I will even do it as a robber... People must be slaves to life."

I thought maybe "Mr. Lu" would go crazy, but he didn't go crazy, because later, I met him again and again at the entrance of that little teahouse on the street corner. He had changed his appearance, and maybe he was really "making life better"...

Really! In the third month, when I passed the entrance of that little teahouse, someone told me that Mr. Lu had done something unclear and had been arrested to face a lawsuit.

I understood that maybe this was his "effort" towards life? However, no matter what, I understood him. On the road of life, he was truly a weary traveler covered in dust.

The Story of Raising Birds

— Qi Quan

After my eldest brother returned to the family, he completely changed as a person. The spirit of perseverance, courage, and progress that he used to have could hardly be found at all; on the contrary, he burned incense and chanted Buddha, like an old Buddhist grandmother who cultivates for the afterlife. My father had tried to seize the occasional opportunity when Xian was excited to inquire about his whereabouts during his years of wandering outside, but whenever my father mentioned this matter, he immediately became depressed, and his bloodshot eyes silently stared at a couplet that promoted abstinence from killing and cultivating blessings: that couplet was also specially hung by him in the guest hall. After some time like this, he would quietly slip out of the guest hall, and no one in the family dared to ask about those things again, only wanting him to do happy things. At that time, the family hired a new cook, who liked to raise pigeons. One summer evening, everyone was enjoying the cool in the courtyard, and the cook unintentionally talked about his experience in raising pigeons, and my eldest brother started talking to him. Every day after dinner, he followed the cook to tea houses and searched for pigeons to buy. My father saw that my eldest brother was happy, and he also mustered his old spirits and built a pigeon shed in a corner of the courtyard. Sometimes he went to the tea house, helping my eldest brother carry the pigeon cage, or ran to the countryside a few miles away to release the pigeons. At that time, the pigeons were the supreme guests in the family, and the work of sweeping the shed and hatching eggs was entrusted to the cook, with special instructions for the servants to pay attention to cats and dogs approaching the pigeon shed to harm their peace.

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

The three of us, father and sons, sat in front of the courtyard every day as if it were a job, watching the white animals flying in the air, watching them whisper affectionately on the corners of the roof, watching them raise their children in the shed. At first, it was my eldest brother who was happy to raise pigeons, and everyone followed him, but later everyone became interested. In less than half a year, we were the pigeon shed with the most pigeons in the countryside.

Due to the interest in those little animals, my eldest brother gradually regained his former attitude. The only difference was that he had become a lively, almost mischievous big child. The interest in raising pigeons expanded to raising all kinds of birds. And that cook, he had some experience in raising birds. As long as my eldest brother thought of something, he could talk endlessly about the method of capturing that kind of bird, how to raise it, and what shape it was of the highest quality. Although he had many reckless statements, my father hoped to please my eldest brother. During the years my eldest brother was away from home, he hardly had a smile every year. (To be continued)

Thunder and Lightning Drama Society

Traffic (1300) 6:00 PM to 7:00 PM

Director: Chen Yi

Cast:

Dr. Zhu... Ma Xiang

Dr. Ma... Lin Fei

Ward No. 5

This is where a social drama unfolds.

The hospital's organization is poor. Wealthy people who fall ill and stay in the hospital have several dedicated nurses. Poor people who fall ill and stay in the hospital can shout themselves hoarse without a single nurse coming. Is this a hospital for the masses' well-being? It's simply hell on earth! Even more detestable are the healthy members of the propertied class who pretend to be sick to recuperate in the hospital because they have money, allowing them to have nurses wait on them, play poker, chat and laugh, just having fun!

Patriotic people who were injured for loving their country are sent here for treatment. After the doctor's examination, they say that this person is useless, so they let him die slowly. His pitiful and miserable cries did not move the hearts of the doctors and nurses. They just said that they were used to hearing it and that there was nothing special about it!

The older sister has been sick for several years because she was too deeply traumatized! Her will has completely disappeared! She can only wait for the coming of the Grim Reaper.

The younger sister's toe was injured, so she came here for treatment. When she entered the hospital, the doctor promised that she could be discharged in three days. However, it has been three weeks now, and her toe is still the same as when she entered the hospital. Therefore, the younger sister can't stand this dull and monotonous environment. She hopes to get out of here as soon as possible.

Finally, the older sister took sleeping pills and died! She left a letter to her younger sister, hoping to reform the hospital's poor organization and build a reasonable public hospital to benefit the masses!

National Studies

Hu Zhangzhao's Analects - Learning

Traffic (1300) 9:30 PM to 10:00 PM

The Master said, "To learn and at due times to repeat what one has learnt, is that not also a pleasure?

To have friends coming from distant quarters, is not that also delightful?

To be not displeased when men do not know one, is not that also the part of a superior man?"

There being filial piety and fraternal submission, it is rare for one who has them to be fond of offending against his superiors. There never has been a man fond of offending against his superiors, and at the same time fond of stirring up confusion.

The superior man bends his attention to what is radical. That being established, all practical courses naturally grow up. Filial piety and fraternal submission, are they not the root of all benevolent actions?

The Master said, "Fine words and an insinuating appearance are seldom associated with true virtue."

Movie News

Three Pairs of Artists

Reception for Friends and Relatives at the YMCA Today at 8:30 PM

Zhao Dan and Ye Lucy; Tang Na and Lan Ping; Gu Eryi and Du Mingjie, the three couples originally planned to hold their wedding at the Lasx Dance School on North Sichuan Road, but because the negotiation procedures were not proper, many friends and movie fans were left empty-handed that day.

On the 26th of last month, they quietly went to the Six Harmonies Pagoda in Hangzhou with the officiant, Mr. Shen Junru, to hold the wedding ceremony. According to friends who saw them off, they only stayed in Hangzhou for one night. After returning to Shanghai, they decided to invite friends and relatives to a reception at the YMCA on Baisen Road on the 3rd of this month; however, the plan changed again temporarily. It is now confirmed that they will invite friends and relatives to a tea party at the YMCA today at 8:30 PM, with entertainment.

The entertainment that has been arranged includes: the prelude by the Pathé Records band, the ensemble, solo performance, and singing by the National Conservatory of Music, He Luting, and others. Finally, the three couples will jointly perform the play "In the Reception Room." The script is very interesting, the characters in the play are also six, and they are three pairs of lovers. The screenwriter is said to be Tang Na, one of the newlyweds. It is expected that the YMCA will be very lively today.

"New and Old Shanghai" Has a Booming Box Office

The Star Film Company's great production of the year, "New and Old Shanghai," which broke the silence of the film industry for several months, has been deeply loved by people from all walks of life since its premiere, and therefore, viewers have flocked to it, creating an unprecedented scene. The film's style is unique, with laughter, anger, sorrow, and joy all reaching a fantastic realm, depicting the various faces of people in society under the depressed market. Wang Xianzhai and Shu Xiuwen are best suited to play such roles. It is very interesting to see their two attitudes of pretending to be poor when rich and flaunting wealth when poor. The film is full of gimmicks and laughter. Director Cheng Bugao's skills are indeed extraordinary. Those who have not seen it should watch it as soon as possible.

Star Magazine Volume 5, Issue 2 Published

The Star Bi-Monthly, which is rich in pictures and texts, has seen a significant increase in sales since the release of its one-week anniversary special issue.
